# Chapter 62 — Hospitality Pitch Scripts

## Chapter purpose

This chapter gives field-ready hospitality scripts.

The scripts should sound like a business conversation, not AI agency copy.

---

## 10-second pitch

> The AI Plug helps hospitality businesses use AI to get discovered, answer guests better, handle event inquiries cleaner, create content faster, and follow up more consistently.

---

## 15-second pitch

> We help visitor-facing businesses figure out where AI can help first: guest discovery, event inquiries, social content, approved answers, QR paths, follow-up, or internal staff support.

---

## 30-second pitch

> Most hospitality owners know AI is changing business, but they do not need random tools. They need to know where AI fits: better content, guest questions, private events, catering inquiries, QR paths, staff replies, or monthly improvement.

---

## 60-second pitch

> Hospitality businesses are not just selling food, drinks, tours, events, or experiences. They are helping guests choose the right move. AI can help when it supports that decision — better local visibility, guest FAQs, private event intake, social content, QR paths, follow-up drafts, and owner visibility. The AI Plug helps find the first useful AI move, build it safely, and improve from there.

---

## Visitor visibility pitch

> If visitors are the opportunity, the first question is whether the business is showing up in the situations where visitors make decisions — resort nights, downtown plans, business dinners, family stops, date nights, group outings, or event weekends.

---

## Event inquiry pitch

> Private events and group inquiries usually need date, guest count, timing, budget, room needs, menu needs, and contact details. AI and better intake can help collect those details before your staff has to chase them.

---

## Guest answer pitch

> If guests ask the same questions over and over, an approved answer system can help. Not loose AI. Approved answers, clear handoff, and staff control.

---

## Content pitch

> AI can help your business stop starting from zero every time you need a post, caption, event promo, menu update, short-form idea, or local search page.

---

## Internal assistant pitch

> The first AI system does not have to talk to guests. It can help your team internally with event replies, catering follow-up, social captions, recap notes, promo ideas, or staff scripts.

---

## AI Growth Review pitch

> The review is the safest start if you are not sure where AI fits. We look at visibility, guest questions, event inquiries, content, follow-up, and internal work, then recommend the first useful system.

---

## Chapter 62 field script

> I would not sell you AI just because it is popular. I would look at your business and ask where it could help first — discovery, guest questions, events, content, staff replies, or follow-up.

Bridge question:

> If you could make one part of the guest or event process easier first, what would it be?

---

## Chapter 62 training check

A rep passes this chapter if the pitch sounds specific to visitor-facing businesses.

A rep fails if the pitch could be used word-for-word for any business.

# Chapter 63 — Hospitality Outreach Scripts

## Chapter purpose

This chapter gives cold, warm, text, DM, email, phone, and follow-up scripts.

---

## Cold text

> Hey [Name], I help hospitality businesses figure out where AI can actually help — things like guest discovery, private event inquiries, social content, approved guest answers, QR paths, and follow-up. Not sure if it is a fit, but are you looking at AI for the business yet?

---

## Short cold text

> Quick question — are you looking at ways AI could help with guest questions, events, content, or follow-up this year?

---

## Website-specific cold text

> Hey [Name], I looked at your website and had one thought: there may be an opportunity to make the guest or event inquiry path stronger with better answers, intake, content, or follow-up. Would it be worth a quick look?

---

## Social-specific DM

> Hey [Name], I saw your page and wanted to reach out. I help visitor-facing businesses use AI in practical ways — content, guest questions, private event inquiries, QR paths, follow-up, and internal assistant support. Not a chatbot pitch. More about finding the first useful place AI can help the business move faster.

---

## Event inquiry DM

> Quick thought — if private events, catering, or group inquiries matter for your business, AI can help organize the questions, details, and follow-up before staff has to chase everything manually.

---

## Warm referral text

> [Referrer] mentioned you might be open to looking at AI for the business. I usually start by finding the first practical use case — visibility, guest questions, event inquiries, content, follow-up, or internal assistant work. Want me to take a quick look?

---

## Cold email subject options

- Quick question about AI for [Business Name]
- Is AI on your radar for guest questions or events?
- Practical AI for hospitality inquiries
- Better event inquiries + guest answers
- Not a chatbot pitch — quick business question

---

## Cold email

> Hi [Name],  
> I work with hospitality and local experience businesses on practical AI adoption — not hype, not staff replacement, and not random tools.  
>
> For visitor-facing businesses, the first useful AI move is usually one of these: stronger content, approved guest answers, private event/group inquiry intake, QR paths, follow-up support, or internal assistant work for the team.  
>
> I wanted to ask: are you looking at where AI could help [Business Name] this year, or is that still on the back burner?  
>
> — [Your Name]

---

## Call opener

> Hey [Name], this is [Your Name] with The AI Plug. I’ll keep it quick. I help hospitality businesses figure out where AI can practically help — visibility, guest questions, private event inquiries, content, follow-up, and internal staff support. I’m not calling to sell a random chatbot. Is AI something you’ve started thinking about for the business?

---

## Discovery bridge

> Before I recommend anything, can I ask how guests or event inquiries usually come in today — calls, website forms, DMs, emails, walk-ins, or something else?

---

## After-conversation recap

> Hey [Name], good talking with you. Based on what you shared, I would not start with a giant AI build. The first useful move looks like [recommendation] because [reason]. That would help with [problem] while keeping [guardrail] clear.

---

## Proposal follow-up

> Hey [Name], just checking back on the proposal. I kept it focused on [first useful system], not everything at once. Do you want to review it, reduce scope, or pause for now?

---

## No-response follow-up

> Hey [Name], I do not want to keep bugging you. Should I keep this open, or would it be better to circle back later?

---

## Chapter 63 field script

> Outreach should connect to the type of hospitality business, the guest decision, and one practical AI use case.

Bridge question:

> What specific observation can we make before reaching out?

---

## Chapter 63 training check

A rep passes this chapter if outreach feels specific and practical.

A rep fails if outreach sounds like spam or generic AI hype.

---

# Chapter 64 — Hospitality Objection Handling

## Chapter purpose

This chapter gives objection responses for hospitality owners and managers.

The structure:

1. Acknowledge.
2. Reframe.
3. Tie to the first useful system.
4. Avoid guarantees.
5. Offer a simple next step.

---

## Objection: “We already post on social.”

Response:

> That is good. The question is whether the content is connected to your guest questions, events, local search, offers, landing pages, and follow-up. AI can help create a stronger system behind the posting.

Next step:

> We can review whether content consistency or conversion after attention is the first issue.

---

## Objection: “We already have a website.”

Response:

> That makes sense. Most businesses already have one. The question is whether the website helps guests decide and take the right next step — reservation, private event inquiry, catering, QR path, or contact.

Next step:

> We can review the current site and see where AI or better systems would actually help first.

---

## Objection: “I do not need AI.”

Response:

> That is fair. You may not need AI everywhere. The question is whether there is one place AI could help the business move faster — content, guest answers, event intake, follow-up drafts, or owner visibility. If there is not, we should not force it.

Next step:

> A review can tell us if there is a useful first move or not.

---

## Objection: “I do not want a chatbot.”

Response:

> I get that. A lot of chatbots are bad. We do not have to start with chat. AI might be more useful for content, event inquiry intake, internal follow-up drafts, promo planning, or approved guest answer planning.

Next step:

> Let’s find the best first use case before deciding on chat.

---

## Objection: “Can you guarantee reservations?”

Response:

> No. Reservations depend on demand, location, reputation, timing, guest fit, and the offer. What we can do is build a stronger system for visibility, guest answers, private event inquiries, content, follow-up, and ongoing improvement.

Next step:

> We can focus on what the business can control.

---

## Objection: “Can you guarantee traffic from Where To Go SA?”

Response:

> No. Visibility is reviewed for fit, and visitor behavior cannot be guaranteed. The goal is to create better context, clearer recommendations where appropriate, and stronger inquiry paths without promising traffic or reservations.

Next step:

> We can review whether visitor visibility or AI systems are the better first path.

---

## Objection: “My staff handles DMs.”

Response:

> Good. The goal is not to replace staff. The question is whether AI can support them with repeat work — event reply drafts, approved answers, follow-up notes, content drafts, or inquiry summaries.

Next step:

> Let’s identify one repeated task that would make their job easier.

---

## Objection: “This sounds expensive.”

Response:

> I understand. That is why I would separate the full system from the first useful system. If the larger scope is too much, we can start with a review or one starter system and leave the rest for later.

Next step:

> Do you want me to price the smaller first step?

---

## Objection: “We tried marketing before.”

Response:

> I understand. A lot of marketing feels like activity without a system. AI can help when it is tied to your real guest questions, events, offers, landing pages, content rhythm, inquiry intake, and follow-up.

Next step:

> Let’s review whether marketing itself was the issue or the system behind it.

---

## Objection: “We are too busy.”

Response:

> That is exactly why the first step should reduce work, not add work. The first system should support content prep, event inquiry intake, follow-up drafts, or approved answers — not create another platform to babysit.

Next step:

> Let’s pick one area that would save time first.

---

## Objection: “We are too small for this.”

Response:

> You may not need a full system. Smaller hospitality businesses usually benefit from one practical AI use case first — content support, event inquiry intake, guest answer prep, or internal follow-up drafts.

Next step:

> Let’s look at the smallest useful first move.

---

## Objection: “What if AI gives the wrong answer?”

Response:

> That is the right concern. Customer-facing AI should use approved answers, boundaries, and human handoff. In some cases, the better first move is internal AI support before AI ever talks to guests.

Next step:

> Let’s identify what answers are safe, what requires staff, and what should never be automated.

---

## Chapter 64 field script

> I hear you. The safer way to look at this is not “do you need AI everywhere?” It is “is there one place AI can help the business move faster without creating risk?”

Bridge question:

> Would starting with a review or one smaller system make more sense?

---

## Chapter 64 training check

A rep passes this chapter if they handle objections without promising reservations, traffic, or revenue.

A rep fails if they guarantee visitor traffic or push public AI without approval.

---

# Chapter 65 — Hospitality Pricing Logic

## Chapter purpose

This chapter translates the master pricing framework into hospitality.

Pricing should reflect strategy, implementation, content, guest-answer approval, event intake, workflows, and ongoing support.

---

## Recommended offer ranges

### Hospitality AI Growth Review

Recommended setup:

**$497 – $1,500**

Best starting target:

**$750 – $1,000**

Use when the owner is unsure where AI fits.

Includes:
- website/visibility review
- social/content review
- guest question review
- event/private party/catering inquiry review
- internal assistant opportunity review
- first useful system recommendation

---

### AI Marketing System / Content + Social Media Engine

Recommended setup:

**$1,500 – $6,000+**

Monthly:

**$750 – $4,000+**

Use when visibility, content, social rhythm, local SEO, AI search visibility, or campaign content is the main opportunity.

Price increases with:
- many platforms
- high post volume
- blogs/pages
- short-form video scripts
- graphics
- event campaigns
- scheduling
- paid social support
- resort/visitor context strategy

---

### SEO + AI Search Visibility

Recommended setup:

**$1,500 – $7,500+**

Monthly:

**$750 – $3,500+**

Use when local visibility, category search, private event pages, visitor-facing pages, and AI search visibility matter.

Guardrail:
No ranking guarantees.

---

### Paid Campaign + Landing Page System

Recommended setup:

**$1,500 – $7,500+**

Monthly management:

**$750 – $3,500+**

Ad spend:
Separate.

Use when the business has a clear offer, event campaign, private party funnel, catering funnel, or promotion.

Guardrail:
No reservation, event booking, traffic, revenue, or ad ROI guarantees.

---

### AI Customer Experience Starter

Recommended setup:

**$2,500 – $10,000+**

Monthly:

**$500 – $2,500+**

Use when approved guest answers, AI chat/operator, concierge guidance, QR help, or voice planning is needed.

Price increases with:
- many answer categories
- menu/event complexity
- multiple locations
- voice planning
- QR flows
- frequent updates
- staff handoff rules

---

### Event / Group / Catering Intake System

Recommended setup:

**$1,500 – $8,000+**

Monthly:

**$250 – $2,000+**

Use when private events, catering, group dining, or guest requests are messy.

Price increases with:
- multiple inquiry types
- package/menu complexity
- routing rules
- alerts
- follow-up automation
- dashboard integration
- file/menu attachments
- approval requirements

---

### Internal AI Assistant Starter

Recommended setup:

**$1,500 – $10,000+**

Monthly:

**$500 – $3,000+**

Use when staff/owner repeat work can be supported internally.

Examples:
- event reply assistant
- catering response assistant
- content assistant
- promo planning assistant
- review response assistant
- monthly recap assistant

---

### Full Hospitality AI Growth System

Recommended setup:

**$7,500 – $35,000+**

Monthly:

**$1,500 – $7,500+**

Use when multiple pieces need to connect:
- marketing
- local visibility
- guest answers
- event intake
- QR paths
- internal assistants
- owner visibility
- ongoing management

---

## Hospitality pricing drivers

Price increases with:

- number of locations
- number of guest segments
- number of inquiry types
- event/private dining complexity
- catering/menu complexity
- content volume
- social platform volume
- landing page count
- paid campaign support
- AI-answer approval burden
- QR path complexity
- routing rules
- CRM/dashboard integration
- voice planning
- launch QA
- monthly support

---

## Chapter 65 field script

> Pricing depends on whether we are doing a review, one starter system, or a full connected hospitality AI growth system. Event intake is different from content, and both are different from a full guest-answer and monthly management system.

Bridge question:

> Do you want the smallest useful first move priced, or the bigger system that could eventually connect everything?

---

## Chapter 65 training check

A rep passes this chapter if they explain price by scope and complexity.

A rep fails if they quote randomly without discovery.

---

# Chapter 66 — Hospitality Proposal + Handoff Templates

## Chapter purpose

This chapter gives proposal and internal handoff templates for hospitality.

---

## Proposal structure

Every hospitality proposal should include:

1. Business summary
2. Problem diagnosed
3. Recommended first system
4. Why this comes first
5. Scope included
6. Scope excluded
7. Required approvals
8. Timeline estimate
9. Setup price
10. Monthly price if applicable
11. Pass-through costs
12. Guardrails
13. Next step

---

## Hospitality AI Growth Review proposal summary

> Based on our conversation, the safest first step is a Hospitality AI Growth Review. We will review how guests discover the business, what questions they ask, how event or group inquiries come in, where content is inconsistent, and where AI could help first. The result is a recommendation for the first useful AI system, not a giant package by default.

---

## AI Marketing proposal summary

> We recommend starting with an AI Marketing System because the main opportunity appears to be visibility and content. The system will help turn your atmosphere, guest questions, events, location, offers, and best-use occasions into stronger pages, posts, local SEO content, and campaign assets.

---

## AI Customer Experience proposal summary

> We recommend starting with an AI Customer Experience Starter because guests ask repeat questions before taking action. The system will create approved answer language, boundaries, and handoff rules so guests can get clearer guidance without AI replacing staff judgment.

---

## Event / Group / Catering Intake proposal summary

> We recommend starting with an Event / Group / Catering Intake System because the main issue appears to be incomplete or scattered inquiries. This system will focus on collecting date, guest count, timing, event type, budget range, contact details, and special needs so staff can follow up faster.

---

## Internal AI Assistant proposal summary

> We recommend starting with an Internal AI Assistant because the owner/team repeats internal work that AI can help prepare. The assistant may support event replies, catering follow-up, content drafts, promo planning, review responses, or monthly recap notes while people remain in control.

---

## Full Hospitality AI Growth System proposal summary

> Your business appears to have multiple connected opportunities: visibility, guest answers, event inquiry intake, content, follow-up, internal work, and owner visibility. We recommend a phased Full Hospitality AI Growth System, beginning with the first useful system and expanding only where it makes business sense.

---

## Scope exclusions

Use these exclusions where relevant:

- no guaranteed reservations
- no guaranteed traffic
- no guaranteed visitor placement
- no guaranteed revenue
- no guaranteed rankings
- no guaranteed reviews
- no guaranteed event bookings
- no guaranteed social reach
- no automatic customer-facing messages without approval
- no AI replacing staff
- no public recommendations without approval/fit
- ad spend separate
- third-party software separate

---

## Internal handoff template

Use after the sale or serious discovery call:

- Business name:
- Contact:
- Business type:
- Location / area:
- Visitor segment:
- Current website:
- Current social links:
- Current inquiry sources:
- Main problem:
- Owner/manager exact words:
- Recommended first system:
- Why this fits:
- What should wait:
- Event/private party details needed:
- Guest answer needs:
- QR/campaign needs:
- Routing rules:
- Staff/owner alerts:
- Current software:
- AI answer approval needs:
- Safe-claims concerns:
- Pricing discussed:
- Next action:
- Follow-up date:

---

## Chapter 66 field script

> I’ll write the proposal around the first useful system, not a vague AI package. It will say what problem we are solving, what is included, what is excluded, what must be approved, and what the next step is.

Bridge question:

> Should I include the larger future phase as an option, or keep this focused only on the starter system?

---

## Chapter 66 training check

A rep passes this chapter if the proposal protects scope and hospitality guardrails.

A rep fails if the proposal sounds like a generic marketing package.

---

# Chapter 67 — Hospitality Delivery + Launch SOP

## Chapter purpose

This chapter gives the delivery team the operational handoff needed to build safely.

---

## Intake checklist

Collect:

- business name
- owner/manager contact
- phone/email
- website/social links
- location(s)
- business type
- ideal guests
- guest segments
- key offers
- events/private party/catering needs
- current inquiry sources
- current forms
- current reservation/event tools
- current CRM/software
- staff roles
- routing destinations
- QR needs
- guest FAQ needs
- menu/package files
- pricing/package language boundaries
- availability language boundaries
- approval contact
- public do-not-say list
- brand tone
- photo/video assets
- Google Business Profile link
- review/follow-up process

---

## Build checklist

Depending on scope:

### Website / landing pages
- experience copy
- event/private party pages
- catering pages
- offer pages
- CTA buttons
- inquiry path
- mobile layout
- trust proof
- safe claims
- SEO metadata
- no fake guarantees

### Event / group intake
- form fields
- date/time
- guest count
- event type
- budget range if appropriate
- package/menu questions
- contact method
- routing
- confirmation message
- consent language
- internal alert
- dashboard/source tags if scoped

### AI Customer Experience
- approved answer library
- guest FAQ categories
- do-not-say list
- handoff triggers
- availability boundary language
- pricing/package boundary language
- event policy boundaries
- test questions
- fail-safe answer

### Internal assistant
- purpose
- knowledge base
- prompt rules
- templates
- output examples
- staff instructions
- approval rules
- update process

### Owner visibility
- new inquiries
- follow-up status
- request type
- source
- guest segment
- notes
- monthly recap inputs
- next recommended improvement

---

## Launch QA checklist

Before launch:

- test mobile layout
- test desktop layout
- test all buttons
- test forms
- test QR path if included
- test alerts
- test confirmation message
- test dashboard entry if included
- test owner/staff routing
- test AI answers with approved questions
- test AI refusal/handoff for unsafe questions
- confirm no guarantees appear publicly
- confirm phone/email/location are correct
- confirm event/private party wording is approved
- confirm no fake claims
- confirm no automatic public messages without approval

---

## Post-launch check

Within the first week:

- confirm inquiries are received
- confirm alerts work
- confirm staff knows what to do
- confirm owner can see what matters
- collect feedback
- identify confusing fields
- note repeated questions
- note follow-up issues
- recommend next improvement

---

## Chapter 67 field script

> The build is not done when the page looks good. It is done when the inquiry path, alerts, approvals, AI boundaries, and owner handoff have been tested.

Bridge question:

> Who needs to approve this before it goes live?

---

## Chapter 67 training check

A rep passes this chapter if they understand launch safety and approval.

A rep fails if they treat launch as only publishing a page.

---

## Restaurants

### Owner cares about

- private events

- group dining

- visitor visibility
- follow-up

### Best first moves

- Restaurant Partner Program / visibility review

### Safe rules

- reservations
- visitor traffic
- revenue

- visitor fit

---

## Chapter 68 field script

> Every hospitality type needs its own language. A restaurant hears guests and private dining. A bar hears vibe and event nights. A venue hears date, guest count, and package. The AI system has to match the business.

Bridge question:

> What kind of hospitality business are we talking to, and what guest decision matters most?

## Chapter 68 training check

# Chapter 69 — Hospitality Monthly Recap + Renewal Logic

## Chapter purpose

This chapter teaches how to keep value visible after launch.

Monthly support should not be vague.

It should show what was reviewed, updated, improved, and recommended next.

---

## Monthly recap sections

A hospitality monthly recap can include:

1. What was updated
2. Inquiries received or reviewed
3. Common guest questions
4. Event/private party inquiry issues
5. Follow-up items
6. Content or campaign opportunities
7. AI answer updates needed
8. Internal assistant improvements
9. Owner visibility notes
10. Recommended next improvement

---

## Monthly recap example

> This month we reviewed the inquiry path, guest questions, and follow-up notes. The biggest pattern is that guests are asking about [topic] before taking action. We recommend adding approved answer language for that question and updating the inquiry form to collect [field]. No reservations, traffic, or bookings are guaranteed, but this should make the next step clearer for guests and staff.

---

## Renewal triggers

Renewal or upsell may make sense when:

- new event pages are needed
- catering inquiry needs more fields
- QR paths should be added
- AI answer library needs expansion
- voice/phone planning becomes relevant
- internal assistant needs more templates
- seasonal campaigns are coming
- paid social needs a landing page
- owner wants better visibility
- follow-up workflow needs refinement
- visitor visibility should be reviewed
- reviews/recaps need support

---

## Renewal script

> The first system is live. The next question is whether we keep it as-is or improve the next bottleneck. Based on what we saw, the best next improvement is probably [recommendation].

---

## Upsell script

> This is not about adding random features. The next improvement connects to what showed up after launch: [guest question / missing event field / follow-up issue / content opportunity / owner visibility need].

---

## Chapter 69 field script

> Monthly support should answer: what changed, what did we learn, what needs attention, and what is the next practical AI opportunity?

Bridge question:

> What did the first system reveal that we should improve next?

---

## Chapter 69 training check

A rep passes this chapter if they can explain monthly value without vague retainer language.

A rep fails if monthly support sounds like “maintenance only.”

---

# Chapter 70 — Hospitality Certification Test

## Chapter purpose

This chapter provides a test to certify reps for the Hospitality + Local Experience vertical.

---

## Section 1 — Multiple choice

### 1. What is the best first step for a hospitality owner who is interested in AI but does not know where to start?

A. Full AI Growth System  
B. Hospitality AI Growth Review  
C. Paid social only  
D. Chatbot install  

Correct answer: **B**

---

### 2. A venue says event inquiries come in missing guest count, date, timing, and budget. Best first move?

A. Event Inquiry Intake System  
B. Generic blog package  
C. Full dashboard rebuild  
D. Restaurant Partner Program  

Correct answer: **A**

---

### 3. A restaurant asks if you can guarantee reservations. Best answer?

A. Yes, with visitor visibility  
B. No, but we can improve the system around discovery, guest answers, event intake, follow-up, and content  
C. Only if they buy the full system  
D. Yes, if social content performs well  

Correct answer: **B**

---

### 4. A bar says staff gets repeat questions about vibe, parking, dress, and event nights. Best first move?

A. Approved Guest FAQ / Customer Experience Starter  
B. AI replacement bartender  
C. Review request system  
D. Social-only content package  

Correct answer: **A**

---

### 5. A catering business has slow follow-up after inquiries. Best first move?

A. Event/Catering Intake + Follow-Up Assistant  
B. AI chatbot for all visitors  
C. Public directory listing  
D. Traffic guarantee  

Correct answer: **A**

---

## Section 2 — Short answer

### Prompt 1

Explain The AI Plug to a hospitality owner without AI hype.

Strong answer should include:

- practical AI adoption
- guest discovery, questions, event intake, content, follow-up, or internal support
- first useful system
- no staff replacement
- no guarantees

---

### Prompt 2

Explain why social posting alone may not solve the problem.

Strong answer:

> Social can create attention, but the business can still lose opportunities if guest questions, event inquiries, QR paths, contact details, and follow-up are not handled clearly after someone shows interest.

---

### Prompt 3

Write a safe response to “Can you guarantee visitor traffic?”

Strong answer:

> No. Visitor traffic depends on demand, timing, fit, competition, and guest behavior. What we can do is improve visibility context, guest answers, inquiry paths, content, and follow-up so the business has a stronger system.

---

### Prompt 4

Name three AI Business Assistant uses for hospitality.

Strong answers:

- event reply assistant
- catering response assistant
- content/caption assistant
- promo planning assistant
- review response assistant
- monthly recap assistant
- staff training assistant

---

### Prompt 5

Name three things AI should not promise in hospitality.

Strong answers:

- guaranteed reservations
- guaranteed traffic
- guaranteed event bookings
- guaranteed revenue
- guaranteed social reach
- exact availability without confirmation
- staff replacement
- unapproved public answers

---

## Section 3 — Scenario

### Scenario

A venue receives private event inquiries from DMs, email, and website forms. Staff often has to chase date, guest count, budget, and package needs.

### Required answer

Recommend the first useful AI system and explain why.

Strong answer:

> I would recommend an Event Inquiry Intake System with an internal follow-up assistant. The system should collect date, guest count, event type, timing, budget range, package interest, and contact method, then create internal summaries or follow-up drafts. I would not promise booked events. The goal is to make event inquiries clearer and easier to follow up.

---

## Section 4 — Roleplay

### Roleplay objection

Owner says:

> “I do not want a chatbot.”

Strong answer:

> That is fair. We do not have to start with chat. For many hospitality businesses, the better first move is event inquiry intake, content support, approved guest FAQs, QR paths, or internal follow-up drafts. If customer-facing AI ever makes sense, it should use approved answers and handoff rules.

---

## Final pass standard

A rep passes this vertical if they can:

- speak in guest/event/experience language
- diagnose the first useful system
- avoid guarantees
- explain AI advantage without hype
- recommend safe first steps
- switch language by hospitality type
- write clean proposal summaries
- hand off delivery details clearly
- explain monthly support as ongoing improvement

A rep fails if they:

- promise reservations, traffic, revenue, reviews, or event bookings
- lead with generic AI tools
- push chatbots too early
- ignore hospitality-specific approval issues
- recommend a full system before diagnosis
- cannot explain the difference between marketing, guest answers, event intake, internal assistants, and owner visibility

---

# Part 8 quality-control checklist

Before this section is approved, confirm:

- It follows AI Advantage First.
- It speaks to hospitality and local experience owner reality.
- It preserves useful restaurant/visitor ecosystem depth without becoming only restaurant-listing language.
- It translates AI into marketing, guest response, event intake, internal assistants, owner visibility, and ongoing adaptation.
- It includes discovery, scripts, objections, pricing, proposals, delivery, QA, monthly recaps, hospitality modules, and certification.
- It avoids guarantees.
- It avoids unsafe hospitality-specific claims.
- It is dashboard-ready.
- It can be merged into the complete master manual later.

## Direction lock for this vertical

This vertical follows the corrected AI Advantage First direction.

The AI Plug is not selling professional service firms a generic website, chatbot, intake form, content package, or automation tool.

For Professional Services, the real positioning is:

# The AI Plug helps professional service businesses get an AI advantage before competitors do.

That advantage can show up through:

- stronger authority content
- better AI search visibility
- clearer consultation intake
- approved process answers
- safer customer education
- internal research and proposal assistants
- follow-up support
- owner-visible opportunity tracking
- ongoing AI adaptation
- practical systems that support professional judgment without replacing it

Professional Services require more trust, more caution, and stronger guardrails than many other verticals.

AI should support the workflow around expertise.

AI should not replace professional judgment.

# Chapter 71 — Professional Services Business Reality

## Chapter purpose

This chapter teaches what professional service owners actually care about before the rep talks about AI.

Professional service businesses are trust businesses.

They usually care about:

- authority
- credibility
- referrals
- reputation
- intake quality
- consultation quality
- client education
- process clarity
- follow-up
- documentation
- staff time
- internal research
- proposal or case preparation
- client communication
- professional boundaries
- risk management
- compliance
- not sounding generic

A professional service owner does not usually want flashy AI.

They want AI that helps the firm look more competent, move faster, and protect trust.

---

## Who this vertical includes

Professional Services includes:

- attorneys
- consultants
- real estate professionals
- insurance agencies
- accounting and tax firms
- bookkeeping firms
- medical and wellness practices
- financial-style local service firms
- B2B service providers
- recruiters and staffing firms
- coaching and training businesses
- advisors
- consultants
- agencies that sell expertise
- professional local offices

Some of these are regulated or sensitive. The rep must be careful.

---

## What professional services actually sell

Professional services sell:

- judgment
- expertise
- trust
- process
- clarity
- confidence
- experience
- credibility
- risk reduction
- relationship
- discretion
- professional next steps

AI must support those things.

If AI makes the business sound careless, automated, generic, or risky, it weakens trust.

---

## What prospects need before saying yes

A prospect may need:

- proof the firm understands their problem
- a clear explanation of process
- trust signals
- service fit guidance
- consultation next step
- document checklist
- pricing/process expectations where appropriate
- what the firm can and cannot help with
- what to prepare before a call
- a human professional involved
- safe answers that do not cross into advice

A professional service buyer is often asking:

- “Can this firm help with my situation?”
- “Do they understand my problem?”
- “What happens first?”
- “What should I prepare?”
- “What does the process look like?”
- “Is this trustworthy?”
- “Will I speak to a real person?”
- “Is this advice or just general information?”

The AI Plug should help the firm answer, qualify, and organize those moments safely.

---

## What the owner feels

Professional service owners may say:

- “We need better clients.”
- “We get unqualified consultation requests.”
- “People ask the same process questions.”
- “We need more authority content.”
- “We need to show up better in search.”
- “We need to explain what we do more clearly.”
- “I don’t want AI giving advice.”
- “My staff spends time answering the same questions.”
- “We need help following up.”
- “I need proposal or research support.”
- “We need a system, but it has to be careful.”
- “I want to use AI, but I don’t want it creating risk.”

These are buying clues.

---

## The corrected AI Plug translation

Translate the owner’s words into practical AI advantage:

- If they need authority → AI Marketing System / SEO + AI Search Visibility
- If prospects are unqualified → Consultation Intake + Qualification System
- If process questions repeat → AI Customer Experience with approved process FAQs
- If staff repeats drafts → Internal AI Assistant
- If proposals or research take time → Proposal / Research Assistant
- If follow-up is weak → Follow-Up Assistant + Owner Visibility
- If they are cautious → Professional Services AI Growth Review
- If multiple areas connect → Full Professional Services AI Growth System
- If they need ongoing content and safe AI updates → AI Growth Management

---

## Chapter 71 field script

> For professional services, I would not start by throwing AI in front of clients. I would look at authority, search visibility, consultation intake, repeated process questions, internal preparation, follow-up, and where AI can support the firm without replacing professional judgment.

Bridge question:

> Are you more focused on building authority, qualifying consultations, answering process questions, improving follow-up, or reducing internal busywork?

---

## Chapter 71 training check

A rep passes this chapter if they speak in trust, authority, qualification, and professional-boundary language.

A rep fails if they sound like they are selling a loose chatbot or generic automation.

---

# Chapter 72 — Professional Services AI Advantage Areas

## Chapter purpose

This chapter translates the six AI advantage areas into Professional Services.

The six advantage areas are:

1. AI-Powered Marketing
2. AI Customer Experience
3. AI Intake + Automation
4. AI Business Assistants
5. AI Operations + Owner Visibility
6. Ongoing AI Adaptation

---

## Area 1 — AI-Powered Marketing

### What it means for professional services

AI-Powered Marketing helps firms turn expertise into useful public content faster.

It can include:

- authority content
- educational pages
- service pages
- FAQ pages
- local SEO
- AI search visibility
- consultation landing pages
- blog/newsletter rhythm
- case/process explanation content
- comparison/fit content
- social posts
- short-form educational scripts
- paid campaign landing pages when appropriate
- content repurposing

### Owner-facing explanation

> AI can help turn your expertise, process, client questions, and service knowledge into stronger content faster — without making unsupported claims or giving advice.

### Examples

Attorney:
- process pages
- general educational content
- consultation prep guide
- do-not-say legal advice guardrails

Consultant:
- authority articles
- service explanation pages
- proposal content
- industry insight summaries

Insurance agency:
- coverage education
- process FAQs
- quote-prep checklists
- no coverage promises

Medical / wellness practice:
- service education
- appointment prep
- general FAQ
- no medical diagnosis or advice

Real estate:
- buyer/seller process content
- neighborhood content
- consultation intake
- no guaranteed price/outcome claims

---

## Area 2 — AI Customer Experience

### What it means for professional services

AI Customer Experience helps prospects understand process and next steps using approved answers.

It can include:

- approved process FAQs
- consultation guidance
- service fit guidance
- document checklist guidance
- general education
- appointment guidance
- inquiry triage
- website operator planning
- human handoff rules
- voice planning

### Owner-facing explanation

> AI can help explain process, preparation, and next steps using approved language while professional judgment stays human.

### Important rule

Professional service AI should not provide:

- legal advice
- medical advice
- tax advice
- financial advice
- insurance advice
- professional advice
- diagnosis
- coverage decisions
- legal strategy
- guaranteed outcomes

---

## Area 3 — AI Intake + Automation

### What it means for professional services

AI Intake + Automation helps collect the right details before the firm spends time on a consultation or proposal.

It can include:

- consultation request forms
- qualification intake
- document intake
- appointment request flows
- project inquiry forms
- budget/scope questions where appropriate
- conflict/risk screening prompts where appropriate
- alerts
- routing
- internal summaries
- follow-up reminders

### Owner-facing explanation

> AI and better intake can help collect the details your team needs before a consultation, so the right person can review the request with more context.

---

## Area 4 — AI Business Assistants

### What it means for professional services

AI Business Assistants are often one of the strongest starting points for this vertical.

They can help with:

- research support
- client/prospect summaries
- consultation prep
- proposal drafts
- follow-up drafts
- meeting recap drafts
- content outlines
- newsletter drafts
- SOPs
- training materials
- process checklists
- internal knowledge organization
- daily/weekly briefs

### Owner-facing explanation

> AI can help your team prepare, draft, summarize, research, and organize work faster while professional decisions and client relationships stay human.

This is often safer than public AI because it starts internally.

---

## Area 5 — AI Operations + Owner Visibility

### What it means for professional services

AI Operations + Owner Visibility helps the owner see what needs attention.

It can include:

- new consultation requests
- qualification status
- follow-up due
- repeated prospect questions
- content opportunities
- proposal pipeline
- client prep status
- monthly recap
- next recommended improvement

### Owner-facing explanation

> This helps the firm see what prospects are asking, what needs follow-up, and where the next AI-supported improvement should happen.

---

## Area 6 — Ongoing AI Adaptation

### What it means for professional services

Professional service firms need ongoing AI support because:

- AI tools change
- search is changing
- AI answer engines are changing
- compliance and boundary issues matter
- content needs updates
- internal workflows evolve
- teams need training and guardrails

Ongoing support can include:

- monthly content updates
- approved answer updates
- intake workflow improvements
- internal assistant improvements
- AI search visibility updates
- staff training updates
- monthly review
- new AI opportunity review

### Owner-facing explanation

> The first system gets you started. Ongoing support keeps your AI use practical, current, and safe as tools and client expectations change.

---

## Chapter 72 field script

> For professional services, AI usually helps in six places: authority content, approved process answers, consultation intake, internal assistant work, owner visibility, and ongoing adaptation. The safest first move depends on where the firm loses the most time or trust.

Bridge question:

> Which area would help most first: authority, consultation quality, process questions, internal prep, or follow-up?

---

## Chapter 72 training check

A rep passes this chapter if they can explain AI as support around expertise.

A rep fails if they imply AI should give professional advice.

---

# Chapter 73 — Best First Offer Logic For Professional Services

## Chapter purpose

This chapter teaches the rep how to recommend the right first offer.

---

## Offer map

### If the owner is curious but unclear

Recommend:

**Professional Services AI Growth Review**

Use when:
- owner knows AI matters but does not know where to start
- firm is cautious
- multiple issues exist
- professional boundaries need review
- rep needs to diagnose content, intake, process questions, and internal work first

Field script:

> I would start with a Professional Services AI Growth Review so we can decide where AI can help safely first — authority content, consultation intake, approved FAQs, internal assistants, or follow-up.

---

### If authority and search visibility are weak

Recommend:

**AI Marketing System / SEO + AI Search Visibility**

Use when:
- firm needs more authority content
- website does not explain services well
- local SEO is weak
- AI search visibility matters
- prospects need education before booking
- paid campaigns need stronger landing pages
- content rhythm is inconsistent

Field script:

> The first opportunity may be authority. AI can help turn your expertise, process, and common client questions into clearer pages, articles, FAQs, and search-ready content.

---

### If prospects are unqualified

Recommend:

**Consultation Intake + Qualification System**

Use when:
- consultations waste time
- prospects are not a fit
- key details are missing
- staff needs better prep
- the firm needs document or issue details before a call
- the next step needs to be clearer

Field script:

> The first opportunity may be consultation intake. We can collect the right details upfront so the firm can decide fit and prepare before spending professional time.

---

### If process questions repeat

Recommend:

**AI Customer Experience Starter**

Use when:
- prospects ask the same process questions
- staff repeats answers
- website does not explain what happens next
- approved FAQs would help
- the firm wants AI support but needs boundaries

Field script:

> The first opportunity may be approved process answers. We can define what AI can explain safely, what it must avoid, and when it hands off to a person.

---

### If internal work is the pain

Recommend:

**Internal AI Assistant Starter**

Use when:
- staff drafts similar emails repeatedly
- proposals take time
- research summaries are needed
- consultation prep takes time
- content drafts are delayed
- SOPs or training materials are needed
- public AI feels too risky first

Field script:

> The first opportunity may be internal. AI can help your team prepare drafts, summaries, research, proposals, follow-ups, and content while professional judgment stays with your people.

---

### If follow-up is weak

Recommend:

**Follow-Up Assistant + Owner Visibility**

Use when:
- consultation follow-up goes cold
- proposals need tracking
- staff needs reminders
- owner needs pipeline view
- prospects ask questions after the first call

Field script:

> The first opportunity may be follow-up support. We can help organize next steps, draft approved follow-up language, and make pending opportunities easier to see.

---

### If multiple problems are connected

Recommend:

**Full Professional Services AI Growth System**

Use when:
- authority content is weak
- intake is weak
- process questions repeat
- follow-up is inconsistent
- internal work is slow
- owner wants monthly support
- firm has budget and approval process

Field script:

> This looks bigger than one fix, but I would still phase it. First we identify the highest-value system, then expand into content, intake, approved answers, internal assistants, and monthly improvement.

---

## Chapter 73 field script

> I would not recommend the same first system for every firm. If you need authority, start with content and search. If consultations are messy, start with intake. If process questions repeat, start with approved answers. If staff is overloaded, start with an internal assistant. If you are unsure, start with a review.

Bridge question:

> Which problem would matter most if it improved first: authority, consultation intake, process questions, follow-up, or internal work?

---

## Chapter 73 training check

A rep passes this chapter if they recommend based on the firm’s trust and workflow problem.

A rep fails if they pitch a public chatbot to every professional service lead.

---

# Chapter 74 — Professional Services Discovery Question Bank

## Chapter purpose

This chapter gives practical discovery questions.

The goal is to diagnose before recommending.

---

## Universal professional services discovery

Ask:

- What kind of clients or cases do you want more of?
- What clients or requests do you want less of?
- How do most prospects find you now?
- What do prospects ask before booking?
- What makes a prospect qualified?
- What information do you need before a consultation?
- What follow-up gets missed?
- What process questions do staff answer repeatedly?
- What internal work takes too much time?
- What would AI help with first if it could only help one area?

---

## Authority and marketing discovery

Ask:

- Does the website explain your services clearly?
- Do prospects understand your process before contacting you?
- Do you publish content consistently?
- What questions could become educational content?
- Are you trying to build local authority?
- Are you trying to show up in search or AI search?
- Do you need landing pages for campaigns?
- Are paid ads part of the plan?
- What claims must be avoided?
- Who approves public content?

---

## Consultation intake discovery

Ask:

- How do consultation requests come in?
- What details are usually missing?
- Who reviews them first?
- What makes someone a good fit?
- What makes someone not a fit?
- Do you need documents before the call?
- Do you need a budget/range question?
- Do you need conflict or risk screening?
- Who schedules the consultation?
- What happens after the consultation?

---

## Process answer discovery

Ask:

- What questions do prospects ask repeatedly?
- What can be explained safely as process?
- What would cross into professional advice?
- What should AI never answer?
- What should always go to a person?
- What disclaimers or boundary language are needed?
- Who approves answer language?
- Would an approved FAQ library help?

---

## Internal assistant discovery

Ask:

- What does the team write repeatedly?
- What does the owner or staff research repeatedly?
- What proposals or summaries take time?
- What meeting recaps are needed?
- What content drafts get delayed?
- What SOPs should be written down?
- What training would help staff?
- What would save the most professional time?

---

## Owner visibility discovery

Ask:

- How do you track new consultation requests?
- How do you track follow-up?
- How do you see pending proposals?
- Do you know which questions prospects ask most?
- Do you know which content topics are needed?
- Would a monthly summary help?
- What should the owner see at a glance?

---

## Guardrail discovery

Ask:

- What professional boundaries apply?
- What advice must AI never provide?
- Are there legal, medical, tax, financial, insurance, or compliance concerns?
- Who approves customer-facing language?
- What should never be automated?
- What must always go to a person?
- Do you want AI public-facing, internal-only, or both?

---

## Chapter 74 field script

> Before I recommend anything, I need to understand how prospects find you, what questions they ask, what makes them qualified, what your team repeats, and what AI should never say.

Bridge question:

> Walk me through what happens after someone first asks for a consultation or professional help.

---

## Chapter 74 training check

A rep passes this chapter if they ask enough to identify authority, intake, process-answer, internal-assistant, or follow-up needs.

A rep fails if they recommend before understanding professional boundaries.

---

# Chapter 75 — Professional Services Pitch Scripts

## Chapter purpose

This chapter gives field-ready professional services scripts.

The scripts should sound serious, trust-first, and practical.

---

## 10-second pitch

> The AI Plug helps professional service firms use AI to build authority, qualify consultations, answer process questions safely, support internal work, and follow up better.

---

## 15-second pitch

> We help firms figure out where AI can help first: authority content, consultation intake, approved process answers, internal assistant work, follow-up, or monthly improvement.

---

## 30-second pitch

> Most professional service firms know AI is changing how people search, ask questions, and prepare to hire. The first useful move is usually clearer authority content, safer process answers, better consultation intake, or internal assistants that help staff prepare work faster.

---

## 60-second pitch

> Professional service firms should not use AI carelessly. The right AI system supports trust: better educational content, clearer process answers, consultation intake, internal research or proposal support, follow-up drafts, and owner visibility. The AI Plug helps find the first practical AI use case, build it with guardrails, and improve from there while professional judgment stays human.

---

## Authority pitch

> If trust and visibility are the issue, the first move may be authority content. AI can help turn your expertise and common client questions into clearer pages, FAQs, articles, and search-ready content without making unsupported claims.

---

## Consultation intake pitch

> If consultations are not always qualified, the first move may be intake. Better intake can collect the right details before the firm spends professional time reviewing the request.

---

## Approved process answer pitch

> If prospects ask the same process questions, an approved answer system can help. Not professional advice. Approved process information, boundaries, and human handoff.

---

## Internal assistant pitch

> The first AI system does not have to talk to clients. It can help your team internally with drafts, summaries, research, proposal prep, content outlines, SOPs, and meeting recaps.

---

## AI Growth Review pitch

> The review is the safest start if you are not sure where AI fits. We look at authority, search visibility, consultation intake, process questions, follow-up, and internal work, then recommend the first useful system.

---

## Chapter 75 field script

> I would not sell you AI just because it is popular. I would look at your firm and ask where it can help safely first — authority, intake, process answers, internal work, or follow-up.

Bridge question:

> If you could make one part of the firm easier or stronger first, what would it be?

---

## Chapter 75 training check

A rep passes this chapter if the pitch sounds serious and professional.

A rep fails if the pitch sounds like AI hype or chatbot sales.

# Chapter 77 — Professional Services Objection Handling

## Chapter purpose

This chapter gives objection responses for professional service owners and managers.

The structure:

1. Acknowledge.
2. Reframe.
3. Tie to the first useful system.
4. Avoid guarantees.
5. Offer a simple next step.

---

## Objection: “We already have a website.”

Response:

> That makes sense. Most firms do. The question is whether the website builds authority, answers process questions safely, qualifies consultations, and helps the right prospects take the next step.

Next step:

> We can review whether the first improvement is authority content, intake, approved FAQs, or follow-up support.

---

## Objection: “We do not want AI talking to clients.”

Response:

> That is a smart concern. We do not have to start with client-facing AI. A safer first move may be internal assistant work, content drafting, consultation prep, proposal support, or approved process answers that staff reviews.

Next step:

> Let’s identify whether internal support is the right first AI use case.

---

## Objection: “AI cannot give professional advice.”

Response:

> Correct. It should not. The system should support process, preparation, intake, summaries, drafts, and approved general information — not professional judgment or advice.

Next step:

> We can define the boundary between safe process information and advice that must go to a person.

---

## Objection: “We do not need AI.”

Response:

> That may be true. The question is whether there is one place AI could help the firm move faster — content, intake, summaries, research, drafts, or follow-up. If there is not, we should not force it.

Next step:

> A review can tell us if there is a useful first move or not.

---

## Objection: “Can you guarantee clients?”

Response:

> No. Clients depend on reputation, market, referrals, competition, timing, and fit. What we can do is build a stronger system for authority, intake, follow-up, and internal support.

Next step:

> We can focus on what the firm can control.

---

## Objection: “We already have staff handling this.”

Response:

> Good. The goal is not to replace staff. The question is whether AI can support them with repeat work — drafts, summaries, process answers, consultation prep, content outlines, and follow-up language.

Next step:

> Let’s identify one repeated task that would make their work easier.

---

## Objection: “This sounds risky.”

Response:

> It can be risky if handled loosely. That is why we use guardrails, approved answers, internal-first workflows when appropriate, and human review where judgment matters.

Next step:

> We can start with a low-risk internal or review-first project.

---

## Objection: “This sounds expensive.”

Response:

> I understand. That is why I would separate the full system from the first useful system. If the larger scope is too much, we can start with a review or one starter system and leave the rest for later.

Next step:

> Do you want me to price the smaller first step?

---

## Objection: “We tried marketing before.”

Response:

> I understand. A lot of marketing feels disconnected. For professional services, content needs to build authority, answer real prospect questions, support consultation decisions, and respect boundaries.

Next step:

> Let’s review whether the issue is content quality, intake, follow-up, or fit.

---

## Objection: “Send me information.”

Response:

> Absolutely. I’ll send a short recap focused on your firm: what we heard, where AI may help safely first, the recommended starting point, what is included, what is excluded, and what would be needed to move forward.

Next step:

> I’ll send that over and follow up after you have had time to review it.

---

## Chapter 77 field script

> I hear you. The safer way to look at this is not “do you need AI everywhere?” It is “is there one place AI can support the firm without crossing professional boundaries?”

Bridge question:

> Would starting with a review or internal-first system make more sense?

---

## Chapter 77 training check

A rep passes this chapter if they handle objections without promising clients or advice.

A rep fails if they minimize professional risk.

---

# Chapter 78 — Professional Services Pricing Logic

## Chapter purpose

This chapter translates the master pricing framework into professional services.

Pricing should reflect strategy, authority content, approval burden, professional guardrails, intake design, internal assistants, and ongoing support.

---

## Recommended offer ranges

### Professional Services AI Growth Review

Recommended setup:

**$750 – $2,500**

Best starting target:

**$1,000 – $1,500**

Use when the owner is unsure where AI fits or professional boundaries must be mapped carefully.

Includes:
- website/authority review
- consultation intake review
- process question review
- internal assistant opportunity review
- guardrail review
- first useful system recommendation

Professional services can justify a higher review range than simple local businesses because trust and risk boundaries require more care.

---

### AI Authority Content + SEO / AI Search Visibility

Recommended setup:

**$2,500 – $10,000+**

Monthly:

**$1,000 – $5,000+**

Use when the firm needs authority content, local SEO, educational pages, AI search visibility, newsletters, blogs, FAQs, or landing pages.

Price increases with:
- professional complexity
- compliance review
- content volume
- multiple services
- multiple locations
- research depth
- approval cycles
- paid campaign support

Guardrail:
No ranking, client, or outcome guarantees.

---

### Consultation Intake + Qualification System

Recommended setup:

**$2,500 – $10,000+**

Monthly:

**$500 – $2,500+**

Use when consultation requests, qualification, document intake, and staff prep need improvement.

Price increases with:
- multiple service types
- document intake
- sensitive data
- routing rules
- CRM integration
- scheduling integration
- compliance language
- dashboard integration

---

### AI Customer Experience Starter

Recommended setup:

**$3,500 – $12,000+**

Monthly:

**$750 – $3,500+**

Use when approved process answers, FAQs, website operator, or voice planning is needed.

Price increases with:
- regulated advice boundaries
- many answer categories
- multiple services
- voice planning
- handoff rules
- approval burden
- frequent updates

---

### Internal AI Assistant Starter

Recommended setup:

**$2,500 – $15,000+**

Monthly:

**$750 – $5,000+**

Use when staff/owner repeat work can be supported internally.

Examples:
- research assistant
- proposal assistant
- consultation prep assistant
- follow-up assistant
- content assistant
- SOP/training assistant
- meeting recap assistant

---

### Full Professional Services AI Growth System

Recommended setup:

**$10,000 – $50,000+**

Monthly:

**$2,500 – $10,000+**

Use when multiple pieces need to connect:
- authority content
- website/landing pages
- consultation intake
- approved process answers
- internal assistants
- owner visibility
- ongoing management

---

## Professional services pricing drivers

Price increases with:

- professional risk
- regulated language
- number of services
- number of decision makers
- approval cycles
- content depth
- research needs
- intake complexity
- document handling
- CRM/scheduling integration
- approved answer complexity
- internal assistant scope
- monthly support
- AI search visibility needs
- staff training needs

---

## Chapter 78 field script

> Pricing depends on whether we are doing a review, one starter system, or a full professional AI growth system. Professional services require more care because authority, approvals, boundaries, intake, and internal support matter.

Bridge question:

> Do you want the smallest useful first move priced, or the larger system that could eventually connect authority, intake, approved answers, and internal assistants?

---

## Chapter 78 training check

A rep passes this chapter if they explain price by scope, trust, and risk.

A rep fails if they price professional services like a cheap website project.

---

# Chapter 79 — Professional Services Proposal + Handoff Templates

## Chapter purpose

This chapter gives proposal and internal handoff templates for professional services.

---

## Proposal structure

Every professional services proposal should include:

1. Firm summary
2. Problem diagnosed
3. Recommended first system
4. Why this comes first
5. Scope included
6. Scope excluded
7. Professional guardrails
8. Required approvals
9. Timeline estimate
10. Setup price
11. Monthly price if applicable
12. Pass-through costs
13. Next step

---

## Professional Services AI Growth Review proposal summary

> Based on our conversation, the safest first step is a Professional Services AI Growth Review. We will review how prospects find the firm, what process questions they ask, how consultation requests are qualified, where internal work repeats, and where AI could help safely first. The result is a recommendation for the first useful AI system, not a giant package by default.

---

## Authority Content proposal summary

> We recommend starting with an AI Authority Content System because the main opportunity appears to be trust and visibility. The system will help turn your expertise, process, client questions, and service knowledge into stronger pages, FAQs, articles, and search-ready content while staying inside approved claims and boundaries.

---

## Consultation Intake proposal summary

> We recommend starting with a Consultation Intake + Qualification System because the firm needs better context before spending professional time. This system will collect the right details, documents, fit indicators, and next-step information so the team can review requests more efficiently.

---

## AI Customer Experience proposal summary

> We recommend starting with an AI Customer Experience Starter because prospects ask repeat process questions before taking action. The system will create approved process answers, boundaries, and handoff rules so prospects can get clearer guidance without AI providing professional advice.

---

## Internal AI Assistant proposal summary

> We recommend starting with an Internal AI Assistant because the owner/team repeats internal work that AI can help prepare. The assistant may support research summaries, consultation prep, proposal drafts, follow-up language, content outlines, SOPs, or meeting recaps while professional judgment remains human.

---

## Full Professional Services AI Growth System proposal summary

> Your firm appears to have multiple connected opportunities: authority content, consultation intake, process questions, follow-up, internal work, and owner visibility. We recommend a phased Full Professional Services AI Growth System, beginning with the first useful system and expanding only where it makes business sense.

---

## Scope exclusions

Use these exclusions where relevant:

- no guaranteed clients
- no guaranteed leads
- no guaranteed rankings
- no guaranteed revenue
- no guaranteed case/project outcomes
- no legal/medical/tax/financial/insurance/professional advice by AI
- no AI replacing professionals or staff
- no automatic customer-facing messages without approval
- no unsupervised public AI answers
- ad spend separate
- third-party software separate

---

## Internal handoff template

Use after the sale or serious discovery call:

- Firm name:
- Contact:
- Professional category:
- Location / market:
- Current website:
- Current social/search presence:
- Current inquiry sources:
- Main problem:
- Owner/manager exact words:
- Recommended first system:
- Why this fits:
- What should wait:
- Consultation details needed:
- Process answer needs:
- Internal assistant needs:
- Routing rules:
- Staff/owner alerts:
- Current software:
- AI answer approval needs:
- Professional guardrail concerns:
- Pricing discussed:
- Next action:
- Follow-up date:

---

## Chapter 79 field script

> I’ll write the proposal around the first useful system, not a vague AI package. It will say what problem we are solving, what is included, what is excluded, what must be approved, what AI will not do, and what the next step is.

Bridge question:

> Should I include the larger future phase as an option, or keep this focused only on the starter system?

---

## Chapter 79 training check

A rep passes this chapter if the proposal protects scope, approval, and professional boundaries.

A rep fails if the proposal sounds like generic automation.

---

# Chapter 80 — Professional Services Delivery + Launch SOP

## Chapter purpose

This chapter gives the delivery team the operational handoff needed to build safely.

---

## Intake checklist

Collect:

- firm name
- owner/contact
- phone/email
- website/social links
- professional category
- services offered
- services not offered
- ideal clients
- not-fit clients
- locations/markets
- current inquiry sources
- current forms
- current CRM/software
- scheduling process
- staff roles
- routing destinations
- consultation qualification needs
- document intake needs
- process FAQ needs
- professional boundaries
- approval contact
- customer-facing do-not-say list
- brand tone
- existing content/assets
- Google Business Profile link
- review/referral process

---

## Build checklist

Depending on scope:

### Website / authority content
- service pages
- authority pages
- FAQ pages
- consultation pages
- process pages
- CTA buttons
- inquiry path
- mobile layout
- trust proof
- safe claims
- SEO metadata
- no unsupported outcomes

### Consultation intake
- form fields
- service/category selection
- fit questions
- document needs
- preferred contact method
- routing
- confirmation message
- consent language
- internal alert
- dashboard/source tags if scoped

### AI Customer Experience
- approved answer library
- process FAQ categories
- do-not-say list
- handoff triggers
- professional advice boundaries
- disclaimer/boundary language
- test questions
- fail-safe answer

### Internal assistant
- purpose
- knowledge base
- prompt rules
- templates
- output examples
- staff instructions
- approval rules
- update process

### Owner visibility
- new inquiries
- qualification status
- follow-up status
- request type
- source
- notes
- monthly recap inputs
- next recommended improvement

---

## Launch QA checklist

Before launch:

- test mobile layout
- test desktop layout
- test all buttons
- test forms
- test document upload if included
- test alerts
- test confirmation message
- test dashboard entry if included
- test owner/staff routing
- test AI answers with approved questions
- test AI refusal/handoff for advice-seeking questions
- confirm no guarantees appear publicly
- confirm phone/email/location are correct
- confirm professional boundary wording is approved
- confirm no unsupported claims
- confirm no automatic public messages without approval

---

## Post-launch check

Within the first week:

- confirm inquiries are received
- confirm alerts work
- confirm staff knows what to do
- confirm owner can see what matters
- collect feedback
- identify confusing fields
- note repeated questions
- note follow-up issues
- recommend next improvement

---

## Chapter 80 field script

> The build is not done when the page looks good. It is done when the inquiry path, approvals, professional boundaries, AI handoff rules, and owner/staff workflow have been tested.

Bridge question:

> Who needs to approve this before it goes live?

---

## Chapter 80 training check

A rep passes this chapter if they understand professional safety and approval.

A rep fails if they treat launch as only publishing a page.

- Consultation Intake
- Approved Process FAQ
- Internal Research / Draft Assistant

### Safe rules

> For law firms, AI should support authority content, consultation intake, approved process answers, and internal prep — not give legal advice.

# Chapter 82 — Professional Services Monthly Recap + Renewal Logic

## Chapter purpose

This chapter teaches how to keep value visible after launch.

Monthly support should not be vague.

It should show what was reviewed, updated, improved, and recommended next.

---

## Monthly recap sections

A professional services monthly recap can include:

1. What was updated
2. Inquiries received or reviewed
3. Common prospect questions
4. Consultation intake issues
5. Follow-up items
6. Content or authority opportunities
7. Approved answer updates needed
8. Internal assistant improvements
9. Owner visibility notes
10. Recommended next improvement

---

## Monthly recap example

> This month we reviewed the inquiry path, prospect questions, and follow-up notes. The biggest pattern is that prospects are asking about [topic] before taking action. We recommend adding approved process-answer language for that question and updating the intake form to collect [field]. No clients, rankings, revenue, or professional outcomes are guaranteed, but this should make the next step clearer for prospects and staff.

---

## Renewal triggers

Renewal or upsell may make sense when:

- new service pages are needed
- authority content should expand
- consultation intake needs more fields
- approved FAQ library needs expansion
- voice/phone planning becomes relevant
- internal assistant needs more templates
- proposal assistant is needed
- paid campaigns need landing pages
- owner wants better visibility
- follow-up workflow needs refinement
- AI search visibility should improve
- staff needs training

---

## Renewal script

> The first system is live. The next question is whether we keep it as-is or improve the next bottleneck. Based on what we saw, the best next improvement is probably [recommendation].

---

## Upsell script

> This is not about adding random features. The next improvement connects to what showed up after launch: [prospect question / missing intake field / follow-up issue / authority content opportunity / internal assistant need].

---

## Chapter 82 field script

> Monthly support should answer: what changed, what did we learn, what needs attention, and what is the next practical AI opportunity?

Bridge question:

> What did the first system reveal that we should improve next?

---

## Chapter 82 training check

A rep passes this chapter if they can explain monthly value without vague retainer language.

A rep fails if monthly support sounds like “maintenance only.”

---

# Chapter 83 — Professional Services Certification Test

## Chapter purpose

This chapter provides a test to certify reps for the Professional Services vertical.

---

## Section 1 — Multiple choice

### 1. What is the best first step for a professional services owner who is interested in AI but does not know where to start?

A. Full AI Growth System  
B. Professional Services AI Growth Review  
C. Paid ads only  
D. Public chatbot install  

Correct answer: **B**

---

### 2. A firm says consultations are often unqualified and missing context. Best first move?

A. Consultation Intake + Qualification System  
B. Generic social content  
C. Full dashboard rebuild  
D. Restaurant Partner Program  

Correct answer: **A**

---

### 3. A law firm asks if AI can answer legal questions. Best answer?

A. Yes, AI can answer legal questions  
B. AI should not provide legal advice; it can support approved process information, intake, and internal prep  
C. Only after hours  
D. Yes, if the client signs a form  

Correct answer: **B**

---

### 4. A consultant needs help turning expertise into content and search visibility. Best first move?

A. Authority Content + SEO / AI Search Visibility  
B. AI replacement consultant  
C. Transportation intake  
D. Review request system  

Correct answer: **A**

---

### 5. A tax firm has document intake and repeated process questions. Best first move?

A. Document Intake + Approved Process FAQ  
B. AI tax advice chatbot  
C. Guaranteed refund campaign  
D. Generic social package  

Correct answer: **A**

---

## Section 2 — Short answer

### Prompt 1

Explain The AI Plug to a professional services owner without AI hype.

Strong answer should include:

- practical AI adoption
- authority, intake, process answers, follow-up, or internal support
- professional judgment stays human
- safe first system
- no guarantees

---

### Prompt 2

Explain why a public chatbot may not be the best first move.

Strong answer:

> Professional services often have advice boundaries. A safer first move may be internal assistant work, authority content, consultation intake, or approved process answers before any public AI answers prospects.

---

### Prompt 3

Write a safe response to “Can you guarantee clients?”

Strong answer:

> No. Clients depend on reputation, market, referrals, competition, timing, and fit. What we can do is build a stronger system for authority, consultation intake, approved answers, follow-up, and internal support.

---

### Prompt 4

Name three AI Business Assistant uses for professional services.

Strong answers:

- research assistant
- proposal assistant
- consultation prep assistant
- meeting recap assistant
- content outline assistant
- follow-up assistant
- SOP/training assistant

---

### Prompt 5

Name three things AI should not provide in professional services.

Strong answers:

- legal advice
- medical advice
- tax advice
- financial advice
- insurance advice
- professional judgment
- guaranteed outcomes
- guaranteed clients
- staff replacement

---

## Section 3 — Scenario

### Scenario

An accounting firm receives consultation requests with missing documents and repeated questions about what to prepare before tax season.

### Required answer

Recommend the first useful AI system and explain why.

Strong answer:

> I would recommend a Document Intake + Approved Process FAQ System, possibly with an internal assistant for staff follow-up. The system should collect required documents, deadlines, service fit, preferred contact method, and preparation questions. AI should not provide tax advice. The goal is to make intake and preparation clearer.

---

## Section 4 — Roleplay

### Roleplay objection

Owner says:

> “We do not want AI giving advice to clients.”

Strong answer:

> That is the right concern. We do not have to start with client-facing AI. The safer first move may be authority content, consultation intake, internal assistants, or approved process answers that clearly avoid advice and hand off to a person.

---

## Final pass standard

A rep passes this vertical if they can:

- speak in trust/authority/professional-boundary language
- diagnose the first useful system
- avoid guarantees
- explain AI advantage without hype
- recommend safe first steps
- switch language by professional type
- write clean proposal summaries
- hand off delivery details clearly
- explain monthly support as ongoing improvement

A rep fails if they:

- promise clients, rankings, revenue, case results, or outcomes
- lead with generic AI tools
- push public chatbots too early
- ignore professional boundaries
- recommend a full system before diagnosis
- cannot explain the difference between authority, intake, approved answers, internal assistants, and owner visibility

---

# Part 9 quality-control checklist

Before this section is approved, confirm:

- It follows AI Advantage First.
- It speaks to professional service owner reality.
- It prioritizes trust, authority, qualification, internal support, and professional boundaries.
- It translates AI into marketing, process answers, intake, internal assistants, owner visibility, and ongoing adaptation.
- It includes discovery, scripts, objections, pricing, proposals, delivery, QA, monthly recaps, professional modules, and certification.
- It avoids guarantees.
- It avoids unsafe professional advice claims.
- It is dashboard-ready.
- It can be merged into the complete master manual later.

# The AI Plug Master Manual v3 — Part 10: Restaurants Vertical Update
**AI Advantage First vertical rewrite**  
**Date:** 2026-05-27  
**Project:** Where To Go SA / The AI Plug  
**Public visitor brand:** Where To Go SA  
**Business systems brand:** The AI Plug  
**Manual type:** Full-depth vertical training manual  
**Section covered:** Part 10 — Restaurants
