## Upload note

Do **not** upload this file into the ChatGPT Project folder yet unless space is available and this vertical is being actively worked.

This is a working vertical manual part. After all manual parts are complete, this section should be merged into:

`THE_AI_PLUG_MASTER_MANUAL_V3_COMPLETE_2026-05-27.md`

---

## Direction lock for this vertical

This section updates the restaurant direction to match the corrected AI Advantage First strategy.

Restaurants already have strong earlier sales and collateral work. Do not throw that away. Preserve the useful restaurant-specific depth: private events, catering, guest questions, visitor visibility, QR paths, follow-up, owner visibility, scripts, objections, and sales logic.

But the restaurant program must no longer sound like only:

- a listing program
- a visitor placement offer
- a QR funnel package
- a private-event form
- a restaurant marketing package
- a chatbot install
- a lead-path system

The corrected positioning is:

# The AI Plug helps restaurants get an AI advantage before competitors do.

That advantage can show up through:

- stronger visitor discovery
- better local and AI search visibility
- more consistent content
- approved guest answers
- private event and catering intake
- QR/menu/campaign paths
- internal event reply and follow-up assistants
- owner-visible inquiry tracking
- monthly AI growth support
- ongoing adaptation as AI changes

Restaurants should be sold through two connected paths:

1. **Restaurant Partner Program** — Where To Go SA visitor visibility, reviewed for fit.
2. **AI Restaurant Growth Systems** — practical AI systems for guest questions, event inquiries, content, QR paths, follow-up, and internal support.

# Chapter 84 — Restaurant Business Reality

## Chapter purpose

This chapter teaches what restaurant owners and managers actually care about before the rep talks about AI.

A restaurant owner does not buy AI because it is trendy.

They care about:

- guests in seats
- private events
- catering
- group dining
- table requests
- local awareness
- visitor awareness
- menu interest
- atmosphere
- social media
- reviews
- staff time
- follow-up
- repeat guests
- business dinners
- resort/hotel guests
- downtown/River Walk traffic
- QR/menu paths
- seasonal promotions
- special events
- owner visibility

Restaurants are high-pressure businesses. Staff is usually busy. If the AI system creates more work, it fails.

---

## What restaurants actually sell

Restaurants sell:

- food
- drinks
- hospitality
- experience
- atmosphere
- trust
- occasion fit
- convenience
- local flavor
- group confidence
- private-event capability
- repeat memory
- social proof

The guest is not only asking:

> “Where can I eat?”

They are often asking:

> “Is this the right place for this occasion?”

That occasion may be:

- visitor dinner
- business dinner
- resort guest night out
- family meal
- date night
- group dining
- private party
- catering
- late-night stop
- River Walk night
- Pearl-area plan
- downtown convention dinner

The AI Plug must help restaurants show up better in those decision moments.

---

## What guests need before saying yes

Guests may need:

- location clarity
- vibe clarity
- menu highlights
- dress/atmosphere expectations
- parking/timing guidance
- reservation or table next step
- private event info
- catering info
- group dining details
- budget/price range expectations
- family/date/business fit
- what to order
- how far it is from hotel/resort/convention area
- what happens after they inquire

A restaurant loses opportunity when the guest or event planner cannot quickly understand:

> “Is this the right restaurant for my situation, and what is the next step?”

---

## What the owner or manager feels

Restaurant owners and managers may say:

- “We need more people to know about us.”
- “Visitors don’t know we’re here.”
- “We need more private events.”
- “Catering inquiries come in messy.”
- “People DM us and nobody follows up.”
- “We need better social content.”
- “We need more business dinners.”
- “We need hotel/resort guests.”
- “People ask the same menu or parking questions.”
- “We do not want AI answering wrong.”
- “We’re too busy to keep up with content.”
- “We need a better way to track group requests.”
- “We want to be part of Where To Go SA.”

These are buying clues.

---

## The corrected AI Plug translation

Translate the owner’s words into practical AI advantage:

- If they want visitor attention → Restaurant Partner Program / visitor visibility review
- If they want better local visibility → AI Marketing System / SEO + AI Search Visibility
- If they need content → AI Content + Social Media Engine
- If guest questions repeat → AI Customer Experience Starter
- If private events/catering are messy → AI Intake + Automation
- If staff repeats replies → AI Business Assistant
- If owner needs inquiry view → owner visibility and monthly recap
- If they want ongoing help → AI Growth Management
- If they do not know where to start → AI Restaurant Growth Review
- If multiple pieces connect → Full AI Restaurant Growth System

---

## Chapter 84 field script

> For restaurants, I would not start with generic AI. I would look at how guests discover you, what questions they ask, whether private event or catering inquiries are getting handled cleanly, what content is hard to keep up with, and where AI could help without replacing hospitality.

Bridge question:

> Are you more focused on visitor visibility, private events, guest questions, content, QR paths, or follow-up?

---

## Chapter 84 training check

A rep passes this chapter if they speak in guest, restaurant, private-event, and visitor language.

A rep fails if they sound like a generic marketing rep or directory salesperson.

---

# Chapter 85 — The Two Restaurant Paths

## Chapter purpose

This chapter clarifies the two public restaurant paths so the rep does not confuse visibility with AI systems.

Restaurants can buy or request help through two major paths:

1. Restaurant Partner Program
2. AI Restaurant Growth Systems

They can also need both.

---

## Path 1 — Restaurant Partner Program

### What it is

The Restaurant Partner Program is the Where To Go SA visitor visibility path.

It is designed for restaurants that want to be considered for visitor-facing guide contexts, such as:

- downtown dinners
- River Walk nights
- resort guest plans
- business dinners
- family-friendly meals
- date nights
- local food picks
- rooftop/bar-hopping paths
- airport timing
- convention traveler recommendations
- private dining/event fit

### What it is not

It is not:

- guaranteed placement
- guaranteed listing
- guaranteed traffic
- guaranteed reservations
- guaranteed revenue
- paid inclusion without fit
- public directory spam
- automatic recommendation
- fake review system

Visibility should be reviewed for fit.

The brand trust of Where To Go SA matters.

---

## Path 2 — AI Restaurant Growth Systems

### What it is

AI Restaurant Growth Systems are practical AI systems for the restaurant’s actual workflow.

They can include:

- AI Restaurant Growth Review
- AI Marketing System
- SEO + AI Search Visibility
- AI Content + Social Media Engine
- AI Customer Experience
- Private Event / Catering / Group Inquiry Intake
- QR/Menu Path System
- Paid Campaign + Landing Page System
- Internal AI Assistant
- Owner Visibility
- AI Growth Management
- Full AI Restaurant Growth System

### What it is not

It is not:

- just a chatbot
- just a website
- just a QR code
- just social posting
- guaranteed reservations
- guaranteed event bookings
- AI replacing staff
- unapproved guest communication

---

## When a restaurant needs Partner Program first

Recommend Partner Program / visibility review when:

- visitor discovery is the main goal
- the restaurant fits Where To Go SA guide contexts
- the owner asks about being recommended
- the business is visitor-relevant
- they want resort/downtown/convention/business traveler/family/date-night visibility
- they understand placement is reviewed and not guaranteed

Field script:

> If visitor visibility is the main goal, we can review whether the restaurant fits Where To Go SA guide contexts. That is reviewed for fit, not guaranteed placement or guaranteed traffic.

---

## When a restaurant needs AI systems first

Recommend AI Restaurant Growth Systems when:

- event inquiries are messy
- catering/group requests are missing details
- guest questions repeat
- content is inconsistent
- follow-up is weak
- QR paths are needed
- owner needs visibility into inquiries
- the restaurant wants to modernize operations and marketing

Field script:

> If the issue is private events, guest questions, content, QR paths, or follow-up, then the AI systems path is probably the better first move.

---

## When a restaurant needs both

Recommend both when:

- the restaurant wants visitor visibility
- and the restaurant also needs better inquiry handling
- private events or catering are important
- the public visibility could create inquiries the restaurant must handle well
- owner wants ongoing support

Field script:

> Visibility can create interest, but the restaurant still needs a clean way to handle guest questions, event inquiries, and follow-up. That is where the AI systems path supports the partner visibility path.

---

## Chapter 85 field script

> There are two restaurant paths. One is visitor visibility through Where To Go SA, reviewed for fit. The other is AI systems for guest questions, private events, catering, QR paths, content, and follow-up. Some restaurants need one. Some need both.

Bridge question:

> Are you mainly trying to get discovered by visitors, or are you trying to clean up guest and event inquiries behind the scenes?

---

## Chapter 85 training check

A rep passes this chapter if they can clearly separate visibility from systems.

A rep fails if they imply payment guarantees public recommendation.

---

# Chapter 86 — Restaurant AI Advantage Areas

## Chapter purpose

This chapter translates the six AI advantage areas into Restaurants.

The six advantage areas are:

1. AI-Powered Marketing
2. AI Customer Experience
3. AI Intake + Automation
4. AI Business Assistants
5. AI Operations + Owner Visibility
6. Ongoing AI Adaptation

---

## Area 1 — AI-Powered Marketing

### What it means for restaurants

AI-Powered Marketing helps restaurants create stronger visibility and content around guest decisions.

It can include:

- local SEO
- AI search visibility
- menu/category pages
- private dining pages
- catering pages
- group dining pages
- short-form video ideas
- social captions
- event promos
- seasonal campaigns
- visitor guide content
- paid social when appropriate
- Google Ads when appropriate
- landing pages
- QR campaign pages
- content repurposing

### Owner-facing explanation

> AI can help turn your food, atmosphere, guest questions, location, events, and best-use occasions into better marketing faster.

---

## Area 2 — AI Customer Experience

### What it means for restaurants

AI Customer Experience helps guests get approved answers and guidance before staff has to repeat everything.

It can include:

- approved restaurant FAQs
- menu question guidance
- private dining FAQs
- catering FAQs
- parking/timing/vibe guidance
- reservation or inquiry next-step guidance
- website operator/chat planning
- QR-based question flow
- human handoff rules

### Owner-facing explanation

> AI can help guests get clearer answers about menu, vibe, timing, groups, private events, and next steps while your team stays in control.

### Important rule

AI should not invent availability, guarantee tables, guarantee reservations, provide unapproved menu/allergen answers, or replace staff judgment.

---

## Area 3 — AI Intake + Automation

### What it means for restaurants

AI Intake + Automation helps collect the right inquiry details before staff has to chase.

It can include:

- private event inquiry forms
- catering request forms
- group dining intake
- QR/menu inquiry paths
- table request handoff
- event campaign forms
- email/SMS alerts
- follow-up reminders
- internal event summaries
- inquiry source tracking

### Owner-facing explanation

> This helps collect date, guest count, event type, budget range, menu needs, timing, and contact details before staff has to go back and forth.

---

## Area 4 — AI Business Assistants

### What it means for restaurants

AI Business Assistants support internal restaurant work.

They can help with:

- private event reply drafts
- catering response drafts
- social captions
- short-form video ideas
- menu/FAQ update drafts
- review response drafts
- monthly promo planning
- local partnership outreach
- staff scripts
- guest question summaries
- monthly recap drafts

### Owner-facing explanation

> AI can help your team prepare replies, content, event summaries, promo ideas, and follow-up faster while people stay in control.

---

## Area 5 — AI Operations + Owner Visibility

### What it means for restaurants

AI Operations + Owner Visibility helps the owner or manager see guest and event opportunities.

It can include:

- new inquiries
- private event leads
- catering leads
- group requests
- follow-up due
- repeated guest questions
- QR path interest
- campaign response notes
- monthly recap
- content opportunities
- visitor segment opportunities

### Owner-facing explanation

> This helps you see what guest and event opportunities are coming in, what needs follow-up, and what questions or campaigns are worth improving next.

---

## Area 6 — Ongoing AI Adaptation

### What it means for restaurants

Restaurants can use ongoing support for:

- seasonal content
- menu/offer updates
- event campaign updates
- private dining workflow refinement
- guest FAQ updates
- QR path improvements
- social rhythm
- AI operator improvements
- monthly review
- visitor visibility review
- new AI opportunity review

### Owner-facing explanation

> The first system gets you started. Ongoing support keeps improving guest answers, content, event intake, QR paths, and campaigns as AI and guest behavior change.

---

## Chapter 86 field script

> For restaurants, AI usually helps in six places: marketing, guest questions, private event/catering intake, internal staff support, owner visibility, and monthly improvement. We do not need all of them at once. We need the first one that creates the clearest advantage.

Bridge question:

> Which one would help most first: more visibility, better guest answers, cleaner private event inquiries, easier content, or better follow-up?

---

## Chapter 86 training check

A rep passes this chapter if they can translate AI into restaurant guest and inquiry language.

A rep fails if they only talk about directory placement.

---

# Chapter 87 — Best First Offer Logic For Restaurants

## Chapter purpose

This chapter teaches the rep how to recommend the right first offer for restaurants.

---

## Offer map

### If the owner wants to be seen by visitors

Recommend:

**Restaurant Partner Program / Visitor Visibility Review**

Use when:
- visitor visibility is the main goal
- restaurant fits Where To Go SA audience
- location/food/vibe fits guide contexts
- owner understands fit review
- public page/funnel receives the request

Field script:

> We can review whether your restaurant fits Where To Go SA visitor contexts. That does not guarantee placement or traffic, but it can identify whether visitor visibility makes sense.

---

### If the owner is unsure where AI fits

Recommend:

**AI Restaurant Growth Review**

Use when:
- owner is curious about AI
- multiple possible issues exist
- restaurant needs diagnosis
- owner is cautious
- rep needs to understand visibility, guest questions, event inquiries, content, and follow-up

Field script:

> I would start with an AI Restaurant Growth Review so we can decide whether the first useful move is visibility, guest answers, event intake, content, QR paths, or internal support.

---

### If content and visibility are weak

Recommend:

**AI Marketing System / AI Content + Social Media Engine / SEO + AI Search Visibility**

Use when:
- social content is inconsistent
- website does not show the experience
- menu/category pages are weak
- private dining/catering pages are weak
- local SEO is weak
- paid social needs better landing pages
- restaurant wants more visitor/local discovery

Field script:

> The first opportunity may be marketing. AI can help turn your menu, atmosphere, events, location, and guest questions into stronger content, pages, and campaigns.

---

### If guest questions repeat

Recommend:

**AI Customer Experience Starter**

Use when:
- guests ask repeat questions
- staff repeats answers
- website does not guide people well
- owner wants chat/operator but needs boundaries
- QR/menu help path could reduce friction

Field script:

> The first opportunity may be approved guest answers. We can define what AI can safely answer, what it should never say, and when staff needs to step in.

---

### If private events, catering, or group dining are messy

Recommend:

**Private Event / Catering / Group Inquiry Intake System**

Use when:
- inquiries come through DMs, calls, email, and forms
- date, guest count, budget, menu needs, or contact details are missing
- event manager needs summaries
- follow-up is inconsistent
- private dining revenue matters

Field script:

> The first opportunity may be event intake. We can collect the details your team needs upfront so private parties, catering, and group requests do not turn into back-and-forth.

---

### If QR/menu paths are the opportunity

Recommend:

**QR + Menu Path System**

Use when:
- restaurant uses QR codes
- menu questions repeat
- campaigns need landing paths
- table tents/flyers/receipts should route to offers
- guest follow-up or private event interest can be captured

Field script:

> QR paths should not just open a generic menu. They can guide guests to the right action: menu, private events, catering, specials, reviews, follow-up, or a guest question path.

---

### If staff/owner busywork is the pain

Recommend:

**Internal AI Assistant Starter**

Use when:
- staff writes the same event replies
- manager needs social captions or promos
- review replies are delayed
- follow-up drafts are delayed
- owner wants monthly recaps
- public AI feels too risky first

Field script:

> The first opportunity may be internal. AI can help your team prepare event replies, catering follow-up, content ideas, guest FAQ drafts, and recap notes faster.

---

### If multiple problems are connected

Recommend:

**Full AI Restaurant Growth System**

Use when:
- visibility is weak
- guest questions repeat
- event inquiries are messy
- content is inconsistent
- QR paths need improvement
- owner needs visibility
- monthly support makes sense

Field script:

> This looks bigger than one fix, but I would still phase it. First we identify the highest-value system, then expand into content, guest answers, event intake, QR paths, internal assistants, and monthly improvement.

---

## Chapter 87 field script

> I would not recommend the same first system for every restaurant. If you need visitor visibility, start with fit review. If guest questions repeat, start with approved answers. If private events are messy, start with event intake. If content is weak, start with marketing. If you are unsure, start with a review.

Bridge question:

> Which problem would matter most if it improved first: visibility, guest answers, private events, content, QR paths, or follow-up?

---

## Chapter 87 training check

A rep passes this chapter if they recommend based on the actual restaurant problem.

A rep fails if they pitch Partner Program to every restaurant.

---

# Chapter 88 — Restaurant Discovery Question Bank

## Chapter purpose

This chapter gives practical restaurant discovery questions.

---

## Universal restaurant discovery

Ask:

- What kind of guests do you want more of?
- Are you trying to reach locals, visitors, resort guests, business travelers, families, groups, or event planners?
- How do guests find you now?
- What questions do guests ask repeatedly?
- Do you get private event, catering, or group dining inquiries?
- Where do those inquiries come from?
- What follow-up gets missed?
- What content do you wish you posted more consistently?
- What part of the guest decision is unclear online?
- Where would AI help first if it could only help one area?

---

## Visitor visibility discovery

Ask:

- Do you want more visitors or more locals?
- Are you near downtown, River Walk, Pearl, airport, resorts, or convention traffic?
- What occasions are you best for?
- What makes your restaurant a good visitor recommendation?
- Do you want business dinners, family meals, date nights, nightlife, or private events?
- Are you looking for Where To Go SA visibility, AI systems, or both?
- Do you understand visibility is reviewed for fit and not guaranteed?

---

## Guest answer discovery

Ask:

- What do guests ask before deciding?
- Do they ask about parking?
- Do they ask about reservations?
- Do they ask about dress/vibe?
- Do they ask about menu, dietary needs, or allergies?
- Do they ask about private events?
- Do they ask about group dining?
- What can AI answer safely?
- What should always go to staff?
- What should AI never promise?

---

## Private event / catering discovery

Ask:

- Do you get private event inquiries?
- Do you get catering inquiries?
- Do you get group dining requests?
- Where do those requests come from?
- What details are usually missing?
- Who follows up?
- How fast does follow-up happen?
- Do you have packages or menus?
- Do you need guest count, date, budget, timing, room type, or menu needs?
- What is the biggest friction in event inquiries?

---

## QR / menu path discovery

Ask:

- Do you currently use QR codes?
- Where do QR codes live?
- Do they only open the menu?
- Could they route to private events, catering, specials, reviews, or guest questions?
- Do you want source tracking?
- Do you need a campaign page?
- What action should a guest take after scanning?

---

## Content discovery

Ask:

- Who creates social content now?
- What content is hardest to keep up with?
- What dishes, experiences, or events should be promoted more?
- Do you need Reels/TikTok/Shorts ideas?
- Do you need captions or campaign themes?
- Do you need private event content?
- Do you need local SEO pages?
- Do you have enough photo/video assets?

---

## Internal assistant discovery

Ask:

- What does staff write repeatedly?
- Who writes event replies?
- Who writes catering replies?
- Who handles review responses?
- Who writes social captions?
- What promo planning gets delayed?
- Would staff use drafts if they could review them?
- What monthly recap would help the owner?

---

## Guardrail discovery

Ask:

- Who approves public-facing guest answers?
- What should AI never promise?
- Can AI discuss availability, or should it always hand off?
- Can AI discuss pricing/packages, or only ranges/process?
- Are there menu/allergen/dietary details that require care?
- Are there alcohol, age, safety, accessibility, or event policy concerns?
- Do you want AI public-facing, internal-only, or both?

---

## Chapter 88 field script

> Before I recommend anything, I need to understand how guests find you, what they ask, whether private events or catering matter, what content is hard to keep up with, and what AI should never say.

Bridge question:

> Walk me through what happens after a guest or event planner first reaches out.

---

## Chapter 88 training check

A rep passes this chapter if they ask enough to identify visibility, guest answer, event intake, content, QR, or internal assistant needs.

A rep fails if they recommend before understanding restaurant fit.

---

# Chapter 89 — Restaurant Pitch Scripts

## Chapter purpose

This chapter gives field-ready restaurant scripts.

---

## 10-second pitch

> The AI Plug helps restaurants use AI to get discovered, answer guests better, handle private event and catering inquiries cleaner, create content faster, and follow up more consistently.

---

## 15-second pitch

> We help restaurants figure out where AI can help first: visitor visibility, guest questions, private events, catering, QR paths, content, follow-up, or internal staff support.

---

## 30-second pitch

> Most restaurants do not need random AI tools. They need practical systems around how guests decide: visibility, menu questions, private events, group dining, catering inquiries, QR paths, social content, and follow-up. We help find the first useful system and build from there.

---

## 60-second pitch

> Restaurants are not just selling food. They are helping guests choose the right experience for the right occasion. AI can help when it supports that decision — better visibility, guest FAQs, private event intake, catering follow-up, QR paths, social content, and owner visibility. The AI Plug helps find the first useful AI move, build it safely, and improve from there without replacing hospitality staff.

---

## Restaurant Partner Program pitch

> Where To Go SA helps visitors figure out where to go. The Restaurant Partner Program is for restaurants that may fit visitor guide contexts like resort nights, downtown dinners, business meals, family plans, date nights, or group dining. Visibility is reviewed for fit and does not guarantee traffic or reservations.

---

## AI Restaurant Growth Systems pitch

> AI Restaurant Growth Systems are for the workflow behind the restaurant: guest questions, private events, catering, QR paths, social content, follow-up, and owner visibility. It is not just a listing or chatbot.

---

## Private event pitch

> Private event inquiries need date, guest count, timing, budget, event type, menu needs, and contact details. AI and better intake can help collect those details before staff has to chase everything manually.

---

## QR path pitch

> QR codes should do more than open a static menu. They can route guests to specials, private events, catering, reviews, guest questions, or follow-up paths — depending on what the restaurant wants.

---

## Internal assistant pitch

> The first AI system does not have to talk to guests. It can help your team internally with event replies, catering follow-up, social captions, review responses, promo ideas, or monthly recaps.

---

## Chapter 89 field script

> I would not sell you AI just because it is popular. I would look at your restaurant and ask where it could help first — visitor visibility, guest questions, private events, catering, QR paths, content, or follow-up.

Bridge question:

> If you could make one part of the guest or event process easier first, what would it be?

---

## Chapter 89 training check

A rep passes this chapter if the pitch sounds specific to restaurants.

A rep fails if the pitch sounds like generic local marketing.

# Chapter 90 — Restaurant Outreach Scripts

## Chapter purpose

This chapter gives restaurant cold, warm, text, DM, email, phone, and follow-up scripts.

---

## Cold text

> Hey [Name], I help restaurants figure out where AI can actually help — things like visitor visibility, guest questions, private event/catering inquiries, QR paths, content, and follow-up. Not sure if it is a fit, but are you looking at AI for the restaurant yet?

---

## Short cold text

> Quick question — are you looking at ways AI could help with guest questions, private events, catering, content, or follow-up this year?

---

## Visitor visibility text

> Hey [Name], I run Where To Go SA, a visitor-focused local guide, and The AI Plug, which builds practical AI systems for restaurants. I wanted to ask if visitor visibility or private event/catering inquiries are a priority for you this year.

---

## Website-specific text

> Hey [Name], I looked at your restaurant website and had one thought: there may be an opportunity to make the private event, catering, guest question, or QR path stronger. Would it be worth a quick look?

---

## Instagram / Facebook DM

> Hey [Name], I saw your restaurant page and wanted to reach out. I help restaurants use AI in practical ways — guest questions, private events, catering inquiries, QR paths, content, follow-up, and visitor visibility through Where To Go SA where it fits. Not a chatbot pitch. More about finding the first useful place AI can help.

---

## Private event DM

> Quick thought — if private events, catering, or group dining matter for your restaurant, AI can help organize the questions, details, and follow-up before staff has to chase everything manually.

---

## Cold email subject options

- Quick question about AI for [Restaurant Name]
- Is AI on your radar for guest questions or events?
- Practical AI for restaurant inquiries
- Visitor visibility + restaurant AI systems
- Not a chatbot pitch — quick restaurant question

---

## Cold email

> Hi [Name],  
> I work with restaurants on practical AI adoption — not hype, not staff replacement, and not random chatbots.  
>
> For restaurants, the first useful AI move is usually one of these: stronger visitor/local visibility, approved guest answers, private event or catering inquiry intake, QR paths, content support, or follow-up support.  
>
> I also run Where To Go SA, so restaurants that fit visitor guide contexts may be reviewed for visitor visibility opportunities.  
>
> I wanted to ask: are you looking at where AI or visitor visibility could help [Restaurant Name] this year?  
>
> — [Your Name]

---

## Call opener

> Hey [Name], this is [Your Name] with The AI Plug and Where To Go SA. I’ll keep it quick. I help restaurants figure out where AI can practically help — guest questions, private events, catering, QR paths, content, follow-up, and visitor visibility where it fits. I’m not calling to sell a random chatbot. Is AI or visitor visibility something you’ve started thinking about for the restaurant?

---

## Discovery bridge

> Before I recommend anything, can I ask how guest, private event, or catering inquiries usually come in today — calls, website forms, DMs, emails, walk-ins, or something else?

---

## After-conversation recap

> Hey [Name], good talking with you. Based on what you shared, I would not start with a giant AI build. The first useful move looks like [recommendation] because [reason]. That would help with [problem] while keeping [guardrail] clear.

---

## Proposal follow-up

> Hey [Name], just checking back on the proposal. I kept it focused on [first useful system], not everything at once. Do you want to review it, reduce scope, or pause for now?

---

## No-response follow-up

> Hey [Name], I do not want to keep bugging you. Should I keep this open, or would it be better to circle back later?

---

## Chapter 90 field script

> Restaurant outreach should connect to the restaurant’s situation: guests, visitor visibility, private events, catering, QR paths, content, or follow-up.

Bridge question:

> What specific observation can we make before reaching out?

---

## Chapter 90 training check

A rep passes this chapter if outreach feels specific and practical.

A rep fails if outreach sounds like generic restaurant marketing spam.

# Chapter 91 — Restaurant Objection Handling

## Chapter purpose

This chapter gives objection responses for restaurant owners and managers.

The structure:

1. Acknowledge.
2. Reframe.
3. Tie to the first useful system.
4. Avoid guarantees.
5. Offer a simple next step.

---

## Objection: “We already post on social.”

Response:

> That is good. The question is whether the content connects to guest questions, private events, catering, local search, QR paths, and follow-up. AI can help create a stronger system behind the posting.

Next step:

> We can review whether content consistency or the inquiry path after attention is the first issue.

---

## Objection: “We already have a website.”

Response:

> That makes sense. Most restaurants do. The question is whether the website helps guests decide and take the right next step — reservation, private event inquiry, catering, group dining, QR path, or contact.

Next step:

> We can review where the current site supports the guest decision and where AI or better systems would help first.

---

## Objection: “I do not need AI.”

Response:

> That may be true. You may not need AI everywhere. The question is whether there is one place AI could help — content, guest questions, private event intake, follow-up drafts, QR paths, or owner visibility. If there is not, we should not force it.

Next step:

> A review can tell us if there is a useful first move or not.

---

## Objection: “I do not want a chatbot.”

Response:

> I get that. A lot of chatbots are bad. We do not have to start with chat. AI might be more useful for content, event inquiry intake, internal follow-up drafts, QR paths, or approved guest answer planning.

Next step:

> Let’s find the best first use case before deciding on chat.

---

## Objection: “Can you guarantee reservations?”

Response:

> No. Reservations depend on demand, location, reputation, timing, guest fit, and the offer. What we can do is build a stronger system for visibility, guest answers, private event inquiries, content, follow-up, and ongoing improvement.

Next step:

> We can focus on what the restaurant can control.

---

## Objection: “Can you guarantee I’ll be listed or recommended?”

Response:

> No. Where To Go SA visibility is reviewed for fit. The guide has to stay useful and trustworthy for visitors. We do not guarantee placement or traffic.

Next step:

> We can review whether visitor visibility, AI systems, or both make sense.

---

## Objection: “My staff handles DMs.”

Response:

> Good. The goal is not to replace staff. The question is whether AI can support them with repeat work — event reply drafts, approved answers, follow-up notes, content drafts, or inquiry summaries.

Next step:

> Let’s identify one repeated task that would make their job easier.

---

## Objection: “This sounds expensive.”

Response:

> I understand. That is why I would separate the full system from the first useful system. If the larger scope is too much, we can start with a review or one starter system and leave the rest for later.

Next step:

> Do you want me to price the smaller first step?

---

## Objection: “We tried marketing before.”

Response:

> I understand. A lot of marketing feels like activity without a system. AI can help when it is tied to your guest questions, private events, offers, landing pages, content rhythm, QR paths, inquiry intake, and follow-up.

Next step:

> Let’s review whether marketing itself was the issue or the system behind it.

---

## Objection: “We are too busy.”

Response:

> That is exactly why the first step should reduce work, not add work. The first system should support content prep, event inquiry intake, follow-up drafts, or approved answers — not create another platform to babysit.

Next step:

> Let’s pick one area that would save time first.

---

## Objection: “What if AI gives the wrong menu/allergy answer?”

Response:

> That is the right concern. Customer-facing AI should use approved answers, boundaries, and human handoff. Some menu, allergy, availability, and pricing questions should go to staff or use approved language only.

Next step:

> Let’s identify what answers are safe, what requires staff, and what should never be automated.

---

## Chapter 91 field script

> I hear you. The safer way to look at this is not “do you need AI everywhere?” It is “is there one place AI can help the restaurant move faster without creating risk?”

Bridge question:

> Would starting with a review or one smaller system make more sense?

---

## Chapter 91 training check

A rep passes this chapter if they handle objections without promising reservations, placement, traffic, or revenue.

A rep fails if they guarantee visitor traffic or public recommendations.

---

# Chapter 92 — Restaurant Pricing Logic

## Chapter purpose

This chapter translates the master pricing framework into restaurants.

Pricing should reflect strategy, content, guest-answer approval, event intake, QR paths, visitor visibility, workflows, and ongoing support.

---

## Recommended offer ranges

### AI Restaurant Growth Review

Recommended setup:

**$497 – $1,500**

Best starting target:

**$750 – $1,000**

Use when the owner is unsure where AI fits.

Includes:
- website/visibility review
- social/content review
- guest question review
- private event/catering inquiry review
- QR path review
- internal assistant opportunity review
- first useful system recommendation

---

### Restaurant Partner Program / Visibility Review

Recommended setup or review range:

**$250 – $1,500+** depending on structure

Monthly / partnership:

**Custom**

Use when restaurant wants Where To Go SA visitor visibility review.

Important:
- pricing must not imply guaranteed placement
- visibility must be reviewed for fit
- any partnership package must clearly state what is included and not included
- no guaranteed traffic/reservations/revenue

---

### AI Content + Social Media Engine

Recommended setup:

**$1,500 – $6,000+**

Monthly:

**$750 – $4,000+**

Use when content rhythm, short-form ideas, social captions, event promos, menu/category content, or local/visitor visibility are the main opportunity.

---

### SEO + AI Search Visibility

Recommended setup:

**$1,500 – $7,500+**

Monthly:

**$750 – $3,500+**

Use when local visibility, menu/category pages, private event pages, catering pages, and AI search visibility matter.

Guardrail:
No ranking guarantees.

---

### Paid Campaign + Landing Page System

Recommended setup:

**$1,500 – $7,500+**

Monthly management:

**$750 – $3,500+**

Ad spend:
Separate.

Use when the restaurant has a clear offer, event campaign, catering campaign, private dining funnel, or promotion.

Guardrail:
No reservation, event booking, traffic, revenue, or ad ROI guarantees.

---

### AI Customer Experience Starter

Recommended setup:

**$2,500 – $10,000+**

Monthly:

**$500 – $2,500+**

Use when approved guest answers, AI chat/operator, QR help, or voice planning is needed.

---

### Private Event / Catering / Group Inquiry System

Recommended setup:

**$1,500 – $8,000+**

Monthly:

**$250 – $2,000+**

Use when private event, catering, or group dining requests are messy.

Price increases with:
- multiple inquiry types
- package/menu complexity
- routing rules
- alerts
- follow-up automation
- dashboard integration
- approval requirements

---

### QR + Menu Path System

Recommended setup:

**$750 – $5,000+**

Monthly:

**$250 – $1,500+**

Use when QR codes should route to menu, specials, private events, catering, guest questions, reviews, or campaign pages.

---

### Internal AI Assistant Starter

Recommended setup:

**$1,500 – $10,000+**

Monthly:

**$500 – $3,000+**

Use when staff/owner repeat work can be supported internally.

Examples:
- event reply assistant
- catering response assistant
- content assistant
- promo planning assistant
- review response assistant
- monthly recap assistant

---

### Full AI Restaurant Growth System

Recommended setup:

**$7,500 – $35,000+**

Monthly:

**$1,500 – $7,500+**

Use when multiple pieces need to connect:
- visitor visibility
- local SEO
- content
- guest answers
- private event/catering intake
- QR paths
- internal assistants
- owner visibility
- ongoing management

---

## Restaurant pricing drivers

Price increases with:

- number of locations
- content volume
- number of inquiry types
- private event/catering complexity
- QR path complexity
- guest answer approval burden
- menu/package complexity
- social platform volume
- landing page count
- paid campaign support
- Where To Go SA partnership scope
- routing rules
- dashboard integration
- voice planning
- monthly support

---

## Chapter 92 field script

> Pricing depends on whether we are reviewing visibility, building one starter system, or connecting multiple restaurant systems. Event intake is different from QR paths, and both are different from a full restaurant AI growth system.

Bridge question:

> Do you want the smallest useful first move priced, or the bigger system that could eventually connect everything?

---

## Chapter 92 training check

A rep passes this chapter if they explain restaurant pricing by scope and complexity.

A rep fails if they imply pricing guarantees traffic, reservations, or placement.

---

# Chapter 93 — Restaurant Proposal + Handoff Templates

## Chapter purpose

This chapter gives proposal and internal handoff templates for restaurants.

---

## Proposal structure

Every restaurant proposal should include:

1. Restaurant summary
2. Problem diagnosed
3. Recommended first system
4. Why this comes first
5. Scope included
6. Scope excluded
7. Required approvals
8. Timeline estimate
9. Setup price
10. Monthly price if applicable
11. Pass-through costs
12. Guardrails
13. Next step

---

## AI Restaurant Growth Review proposal summary

> Based on our conversation, the safest first step is an AI Restaurant Growth Review. We will review how guests discover the restaurant, what questions they ask, how private event or catering inquiries come in, whether QR/menu paths are helping, where content is inconsistent, and where AI could help first. The result is a recommendation for the first useful AI system, not a giant package by default.

---

## Restaurant Partner Program proposal summary

> Based on our conversation, the restaurant may be a fit for Where To Go SA visitor visibility review. This does not guarantee placement, traffic, reservations, or revenue. The review looks at whether the restaurant fits useful visitor guide contexts and what kind of visibility or content path may make sense.

---

## AI Marketing proposal summary

> We recommend starting with an AI Marketing System because the main opportunity appears to be visibility and content. The system will help turn your menu, atmosphere, guest questions, events, location, offers, and best-use occasions into stronger pages, posts, local SEO content, and campaign assets.

---

## AI Customer Experience proposal summary

> We recommend starting with an AI Customer Experience Starter because guests ask repeat questions before taking action. The system will create approved answer language, boundaries, and handoff rules so guests can get clearer guidance without AI replacing staff judgment.

---

## Private Event / Catering Intake proposal summary

> We recommend starting with a Private Event / Catering Inquiry System because the main issue appears to be incomplete or scattered inquiries. This system will focus on collecting date, guest count, timing, event type, budget range, menu needs, contact details, and special requirements so staff can follow up faster.

---

## QR + Menu Path proposal summary

> We recommend starting with a QR + Menu Path System because QR codes can do more than open a static menu. The system can route guests to the right next action: menu, specials, private events, catering, reviews, guest questions, or campaign pages.

---

## Internal AI Assistant proposal summary

> We recommend starting with an Internal AI Assistant because the owner/team repeats internal work that AI can help prepare. The assistant may support event replies, catering follow-up, content drafts, promo planning, review responses, or monthly recap notes while people remain in control.

---

## Full AI Restaurant Growth System proposal summary

> Your restaurant appears to have multiple connected opportunities: visibility, guest answers, private event/catering intake, QR paths, content, follow-up, internal work, and owner visibility. We recommend a phased Full AI Restaurant Growth System, beginning with the first useful system and expanding only where it makes business sense.

---

## Scope exclusions

Use these exclusions where relevant:

- no guaranteed reservations
- no guaranteed visitor traffic
- no guaranteed placement
- no guaranteed public recommendation
- no guaranteed revenue
- no guaranteed rankings
- no guaranteed reviews
- no guaranteed event bookings
- no guaranteed social reach
- no automatic customer-facing messages without approval
- no AI replacing staff
- no unapproved menu/allergen/availability answers
- ad spend separate
- third-party software separate

---

## Internal handoff template

Use after the sale or serious discovery call:

- Restaurant name:
- Contact:
- Location / area:
- Cuisine / concept:
- Visitor segment:
- Current website:
- Current social links:
- Current inquiry sources:
- Main problem:
- Owner/manager exact words:
- Recommended first system:
- Visibility path, systems path, or both:
- Why this fits:
- What should wait:
- Private event/catering details needed:
- Guest answer needs:
- QR/campaign needs:
- Routing rules:
- Staff/owner alerts:
- Current software:
- AI answer approval needs:
- Safe-claims concerns:
- Pricing discussed:
- Next action:
- Follow-up date:

---

## Chapter 93 field script

> I’ll write the proposal around the first useful system, not a vague AI package. It will say whether this is visibility, systems, or both; what problem we are solving; what is included; what is excluded; what must be approved; and what the next step is.

Bridge question:

> Should I include both the visitor visibility path and the AI systems path, or keep this focused on one?

---

## Chapter 93 training check

A rep passes this chapter if the proposal protects scope and restaurant guardrails.

A rep fails if the proposal sounds like a guaranteed traffic package.

# Chapter 94 — Restaurant Delivery + Launch SOP

## Chapter purpose

This chapter gives the delivery team the operational handoff needed to build safely.

---

## Intake checklist

Collect:

- restaurant name
- owner/manager contact
- phone/email
- website/social links
- location(s)
- cuisine/concept
- ideal guests
- visitor segments
- best occasions
- private event/catering needs
- current inquiry sources
- current forms
- current reservation/event tools
- current QR/menu tools
- staff roles
- routing destinations
- guest FAQ needs
- menu/package files
- pricing/package language boundaries
- availability language boundaries
- allergen/menu answer boundaries
- approval contact
- public do-not-say list
- brand tone
- photo/video assets
- Google Business Profile link
- review/follow-up process

---

## Build checklist

Depending on scope:

### Website / landing pages
- restaurant concept copy
- private dining pages
- catering pages
- group dining pages
- menu/category pages
- CTA buttons
- inquiry path
- mobile layout
- trust proof
- safe claims
- SEO metadata
- no fake guarantees

### Private event / catering intake
- form fields
- date/time
- guest count
- event type
- budget range if appropriate
- package/menu questions
- contact method
- routing
- confirmation message
- consent language
- internal alert
- dashboard/source tags if scoped

### QR + menu paths
- QR destination pages
- campaign paths
- menu links
- private event/catering CTA
- review path
- guest question path
- source tracking if scoped

### AI Customer Experience
- approved answer library
- guest FAQ categories
- do-not-say list
- handoff triggers
- availability boundary language
- pricing/package boundary language
- allergy/menu boundaries
- event policy boundaries
- test questions
- fail-safe answer

### Internal assistant
- purpose
- knowledge base
- prompt rules
- templates
- output examples
- staff instructions
- approval rules
- update process

### Owner visibility
- new inquiries
- follow-up status
- request type
- source
- guest segment
- notes
- monthly recap inputs
- next recommended improvement

---

## Launch QA checklist

Before launch:

- test mobile layout
- test desktop layout
- test all buttons
- test forms
- test QR path if included
- test alerts
- test confirmation message
- test dashboard entry if included
- test owner/staff routing
- test AI answers with approved questions
- test AI refusal/handoff for unsafe questions
- confirm no guarantees appear publicly
- confirm phone/email/location are correct
- confirm private event/catering wording is approved
- confirm no unapproved menu/allergen/availability answers
- confirm no fake claims
- confirm no automatic public messages without approval

---

## Post-launch check

Within the first week:

- confirm inquiries are received
- confirm alerts work
- confirm staff knows what to do
- confirm owner can see what matters
- collect feedback
- identify confusing fields
- note repeated questions
- note follow-up issues
- recommend next improvement

---

## Chapter 94 field script

> The build is not done when the page looks good. It is done when the guest path, inquiry path, QR path, alerts, approvals, AI boundaries, and owner handoff have been tested.

Bridge question:

> Who needs to approve this before it goes live?

---

## Chapter 94 training check

A rep passes this chapter if they understand restaurant launch safety and approval.

A rep fails if they treat launch as only publishing a page.

# Chapter 96 — Restaurant Monthly Recap + Renewal Logic

## Chapter purpose

This chapter teaches how to keep value visible after launch.

Monthly support should not be vague.

It should show what was reviewed, updated, improved, and recommended next.

---

## Monthly recap sections

A restaurant monthly recap can include:

1. What was updated
2. Inquiries received or reviewed
3. Common guest questions
4. Private event/catering inquiry issues
5. QR path notes
6. Follow-up items
7. Content or campaign opportunities
8. AI answer updates needed
9. Internal assistant improvements
10. Owner visibility notes
11. Recommended next improvement

---

## Monthly recap example

> This month we reviewed the inquiry path, guest questions, QR path, and follow-up notes. The biggest pattern is that guests are asking about [topic] before taking action. We recommend adding approved answer language for that question and updating the event inquiry form to collect [field]. No reservations, traffic, event bookings, or revenue are guaranteed, but this should make the next step clearer for guests and staff.

---

## Renewal triggers

Renewal or upsell may make sense when:

- private event page needs improvement
- catering inquiry needs more fields
- QR paths should be added
- guest FAQ library needs expansion
- social content rhythm needs support
- paid social needs a landing page
- review response support is needed
- owner wants better inquiry visibility
- Where To Go SA visibility should be reviewed
- AI phone/voice planning becomes relevant
- monthly content and campaign support is needed

---

## Renewal script

> The first system is live. The next question is whether we keep it as-is or improve the next bottleneck. Based on what we saw, the best next improvement is probably [recommendation].

---

## Upsell script

> This is not about adding random features. The next improvement connects to what showed up after launch: [guest question / missing event field / QR path issue / content opportunity / follow-up need / visibility opportunity].

---

## Chapter 96 field script

> Monthly support should answer: what changed, what did we learn, what needs attention, and what is the next practical AI opportunity?

Bridge question:

> What did the first system reveal that we should improve next?

---

## Chapter 96 training check

A rep passes this chapter if they can explain monthly value without vague retainer language.

A rep fails if monthly support sounds like “maintenance only.”

---

# Chapter 97 — Restaurant Certification Test

## Chapter purpose

This chapter provides a test to certify reps for the Restaurant vertical.

---

## Section 1 — Multiple choice

### 1. What is the best first step for a restaurant owner who is interested in AI but does not know where to start?

A. Full AI Growth System  
B. AI Restaurant Growth Review  
C. Paid social only  
D. Public chatbot install  

Correct answer: **B**

---

### 2. A restaurant says private event inquiries come in missing date, guest count, timing, and budget. Best first move?

A. Private Event / Catering Inquiry System  
B. Generic blog package  
C. Full dashboard rebuild  
D. Transportation routing  

Correct answer: **A**

---

### 3. A restaurant asks if you can guarantee reservations. Best answer?

A. Yes, with visitor visibility  
B. No, but we can improve the system around discovery, guest answers, event intake, follow-up, content, and QR paths  
C. Only if they buy the full system  
D. Yes, if social content performs well  

Correct answer: **B**

---

### 4. A restaurant wants Where To Go SA placement. Best response?

A. Payment guarantees listing  
B. Visibility is reviewed for fit and does not guarantee placement, traffic, or reservations  
C. All restaurants are automatically listed  
D. Placement guarantees visitor traffic  

Correct answer: **B**

---

### 5. A restaurant has QR codes that only open a menu. Best possible first move?

A. QR + Menu Path System  
B. AI replacement server  
C. Guaranteed traffic campaign  
D. Professional services intake  

Correct answer: **A**

---

## Section 2 — Short answer

### Prompt 1

Explain The AI Plug to a restaurant owner without AI hype.

Strong answer should include:

- practical AI adoption
- visitor visibility, guest questions, private events, catering, QR paths, content, or follow-up
- first useful system
- no staff replacement
- no guarantees

---

### Prompt 2

Explain why visitor visibility alone may not solve the problem.

Strong answer:

> Visibility can create interest, but the restaurant can still lose opportunities if guest questions, private event inquiries, QR paths, contact details, and follow-up are not handled clearly after someone shows interest.

---

### Prompt 3

Write a safe response to “Can you guarantee visitor traffic or reservations?”

Strong answer:

> No. Visitor traffic and reservations depend on demand, timing, fit, location, reputation, and guest behavior. What we can do is improve visibility context, guest answers, inquiry paths, content, QR paths, and follow-up so the restaurant has a stronger system.

---

### Prompt 4

Name three AI Business Assistant uses for restaurants.

Strong answers:

- event reply assistant
- catering response assistant
- content/caption assistant
- promo planning assistant
- review response assistant
- monthly recap assistant
- guest FAQ assistant

---

### Prompt 5

Name three things AI should not promise in restaurants.

Strong answers:

- guaranteed reservations
- guaranteed visitor traffic
- guaranteed placement
- guaranteed event bookings
- guaranteed revenue
- guaranteed social reach
- exact availability without confirmation
- staff replacement
- unapproved menu/allergen answers

---

## Section 3 — Scenario

### Scenario

A restaurant receives private event inquiries from DMs, email, and website forms. Staff often has to chase date, guest count, budget, and menu needs. The owner also wants to be considered for visitor visibility on Where To Go SA.

### Required answer

Recommend the first useful AI system and explain why.

Strong answer:

> I would recommend a Private Event / Catering Inquiry System first, plus a separate Restaurant Partner Program visibility review if the restaurant fits visitor guide contexts. The inquiry system should collect date, guest count, event type, timing, budget range, menu needs, and contact method, then create internal summaries or follow-up drafts. I would not promise booked events, traffic, reservations, or placement.

---

## Section 4 — Roleplay

### Roleplay objection

Owner says:

> “I don’t want a chatbot.”

Strong answer:

> That is fair. We do not have to start with chat. For many restaurants, the better first move is private event intake, catering follow-up, QR paths, content support, approved guest FAQs, or internal reply drafts. If customer-facing AI ever makes sense, it should use approved answers and handoff rules.

---

## Final pass standard

A rep passes this vertical if they can:

- speak in guest/restaurant/event/visitor language
- separate visibility from AI systems
- diagnose the first useful system
- avoid guarantees
- explain AI advantage without hype
- recommend safe first steps
- write clean proposal summaries
- hand off delivery details clearly
- explain monthly support as ongoing improvement

A rep fails if they:

- promise reservations, traffic, revenue, reviews, event bookings, or placement
- lead with generic AI tools
- push chatbots too early
- imply payment guarantees public recommendation
- recommend a full system before diagnosis
- cannot explain the difference between visibility, marketing, guest answers, event intake, QR paths, internal assistants, and owner visibility

---

# Part 10 quality-control checklist

Before this section is approved, confirm:

- It follows AI Advantage First.
- It preserves the useful restaurant program depth.
- It clearly separates Restaurant Partner Program from AI Restaurant Growth Systems.
- It speaks to restaurant owner/manager reality.
- It translates AI into visitor visibility, marketing, guest response, private event/catering intake, QR paths, internal assistants, owner visibility, and ongoing adaptation.
- It includes discovery, scripts, objections, pricing, proposals, delivery, QA, monthly recaps, restaurant modules, and certification.
- It avoids guarantees.
- It avoids unsafe restaurant-specific claims.
- It is dashboard-ready.
- It can be merged into the complete master manual later.

# The AI Plug Master Manual v3 — Part 11: Transportation + Concierge Vertical Manual
**AI Advantage First vertical rewrite**  
**Date:** 2026-05-27

**Public visitor brand:** Where To Go SA  
**Business systems brand:** The AI Plug  
**Manual type:** Full-depth vertical training manual  
**Section covered:** Part 11 — Transportation + Concierge

## Upload note

Do **not** upload this file into the ChatGPT Project folder yet unless space is available and this vertical is being actively worked.

This is a working vertical manual part. After all manual parts are complete, this section should be merged into:

`THE_AI_PLUG_MASTER_MANUAL_V3_COMPLETE_2026-05-27.md`

---

## Direction lock for this vertical

This vertical follows the corrected AI Advantage First direction.

The AI Plug is not selling transportation businesses a generic website, request form, route page, chatbot, or dispatch tool.

For Transportation + Concierge businesses, the real positioning is:

# The AI Plug helps transportation and concierge businesses get an AI advantage before competitors do.

That advantage can show up through:

- clearer route and service visibility
- better airport/resort/event request intake
- faster customer question handling
- safer provider handoff
- internal trip summary support
- route-specific content and local SEO
- voice and phone workflow planning
- owner/operator visibility
- monthly AI growth support
- ongoing adaptation as AI tools and customer expectations change

This vertical requires careful wording.

The AI Plug must not promise transportation availability, guaranteed pickup, dispatch, legal/licensed service, insurance compliance, exact drive times, or automatic provider assignment unless those terms are actually controlled and approved by the client.

AI should support the request and handoff.

AI should not create unsafe or illegal promises.
