# Chapter 113 — Best First Offer Logic For Local Brands

## Chapter purpose

This chapter teaches the rep how to recommend the right first offer for local brands and retail businesses.

---

## Offer map

### If the owner is curious but unclear

Recommend:

**Local Brand AI Growth Review**

Use when:
- owner knows AI matters but does not know where to start
- multiple issues exist
- product/category/brand claims need review
- rep needs to diagnose content, product questions, QR paths, campaigns, and follow-up

Field script:

> I would start with a Local Brand AI Growth Review so we can decide whether the first useful move is content, product answers, QR campaigns, event follow-up, customer interest capture, or internal assistant work.

---

### If content is weak

Recommend:

**AI Content + Social Media Engine**

Use when:
- owner does not post consistently
- product descriptions are weak
- short-form ideas are needed
- promotions need copy
- email/text content is inconsistent
- brand story needs to be turned into repeatable content

Field script:

> The first opportunity may be content. AI can help turn your products, story, customer questions, and promotions into posts, captions, pages, emails, and short-form ideas faster.

---

### If local/AI search discovery is weak

Recommend:

**SEO + AI Search Visibility**

Use when:
- store or product is hard to find
- local search matters
- product/category pages are weak
- customers ask questions that could become FAQ/search content
- AI search visibility matters

Field script:

> The first opportunity may be discovery. AI can help organize product, category, location, and customer-question content so more people understand what you offer.

---

### If product questions repeat

Recommend:

**AI Customer Experience Starter**

Use when:
- customers ask repeat product questions
- staff repeats answers
- pickup/shipping/promo questions repeat
- product selection or gifting guidance is needed
- public AI needs approved boundaries

Field script:

> The first opportunity may be approved product answers. We can define what AI can safely answer, what it should never claim, and when staff needs to step in.

---

### If QR campaigns, pop-ups, or events matter

Recommend:

**QR Campaign + Interest Capture System**

Use when:
- QR codes are used at events, pop-ups, displays, packaging, flyers, or receipts
- product interest is not captured
- follow-up after events is weak
- waitlists, promo signups, or customer preferences matter

Field script:

> The first opportunity may be QR interest capture. QR codes should not just send people to a generic page. They can capture product interest, event signups, waitlists, promotions, and follow-up permission.

---

### If promotion or paid campaign needs a path

Recommend:

**Paid Campaign + Landing Page System**

Use when:
- owner wants paid social or ads
- campaign offer is clear
- landing page is needed
- customer interest or email/text capture matters
- follow-up path is needed

Field script:

> The first opportunity may be a campaign path. Paid promotion works better when the offer, landing page, product answers, interest capture, and follow-up are ready.

---

### If internal work is the pain

Recommend:

**Internal AI Assistant Starter**

Use when:
- owner writes the same content repeatedly
- product descriptions take time
- customer reply drafts are needed
- email campaigns are delayed
- promo planning is slow
- staff needs scripts or SOPs

Field script:

> The first opportunity may be internal. AI can help prepare product copy, captions, customer replies, promo ideas, emails, and SOPs while the owner keeps control.

---

### If multiple problems are connected

Recommend:

**Full Local Brand AI Growth System**

Use when:
- content is weak
- product questions repeat
- QR/event capture is weak
- follow-up is inconsistent
- owner wants visibility
- monthly support makes sense

Field script:

> This looks bigger than one fix, but I would still phase it. First we identify the highest-value system, then expand into content, product answers, QR paths, campaign pages, internal assistants, and monthly improvement.

---

## Chapter 113 field script

> I would not recommend the same first system for every local brand. If content is weak, start with content. If product questions repeat, start with approved answers. If events and QR codes matter, start with interest capture. If paid campaigns are planned, build the landing path. If you are unsure, start with a review.

Bridge question:

> Which problem would matter most if it improved first: content, discovery, product questions, QR interest capture, campaigns, or follow-up?

---

## Chapter 113 training check

A rep passes this chapter if they recommend based on the actual local brand problem.

A rep fails if they pitch generic social media to everyone.

---

# Chapter 114 — Local Brands Discovery Question Bank

## Chapter purpose

This chapter gives practical discovery questions.

The goal is to diagnose before recommending.

---

## Universal local brand discovery

Ask:

- What products or categories matter most?
- What products do you want to sell more of?
- How do customers find you now?
- What questions do customers ask repeatedly?
- What content do you wish you posted more often?
- Do you do pop-ups, events, markets, or in-store promotions?
- Do you use QR codes?
- Do you collect emails/text permissions?
- What follow-up gets missed?
- What part of the customer decision is unclear online?
- Where would AI help first if it could only help one area?

---

## Product and brand discovery

Ask:

- What makes the brand different?
- What should customers understand faster?
- What products need better descriptions?
- What products are good gifts?
- What products need education?
- Are there claims we must avoid?
- Are there regulated product categories?
- Who approves product copy?
- What should AI never say?

---

## Content discovery

Ask:

- Who creates content now?
- What platforms matter?
- What content is hardest to keep up with?
- Do you need short-form video ideas?
- Do you need product captions?
- Do you need email or SMS copy?
- Do you need campaign themes?
- Do you have photos or videos?
- Do you have a monthly content rhythm?

---

## QR / event / campaign discovery

Ask:

- Where are QR codes used?
- What happens after someone scans?
- Do you capture interest?
- Do you collect email/text permission?
- Do you need a waitlist?
- Do you need event signup?
- Do you need product preference capture?
- Do you need source tracking?
- What follow-up should happen after the scan?

---

## Customer answer discovery

Ask:

- What product questions repeat?
- Do customers ask about availability?
- Do customers ask about shipping or pickup?
- Do customers ask about size, color, style, or use case?
- Do customers ask about health, safety, or performance claims?
- What can AI answer safely?
- What should always go to staff?
- Would an approved FAQ library help?

---

## Internal assistant discovery

Ask:

- What does the owner write repeatedly?
- What customer replies repeat?
- What product copy is missing?
- What email campaigns get delayed?
- What social captions are hard to create?
- What SOPs or staff scripts are needed?
- What monthly recap would help the owner?

---

## Guardrail discovery

Ask:

- Are there product claims that must be approved?
- Are there health, wellness, safety, legal, age, or regulated product concerns?
- What should AI never promise?
- Can AI discuss availability or should it hand off?
- Can AI discuss price/promos or only approved offers?
- Who approves public-facing answers?
- Do you want AI public-facing, internal-only, or both?

---

## Chapter 114 field script

> Before I recommend anything, I need to understand what products matter, how customers find you, what they ask, what content is hard to create, how events or QR codes work, and what AI should never claim.

Bridge question:

> Walk me through what happens after someone first discovers a product or asks a question.

---

## Chapter 114 training check

A rep passes this chapter if they ask enough to identify content, product answer, QR campaign, discovery, or internal assistant needs.

A rep fails if they recommend before understanding the brand and product claims.

---

# Chapter 115 — Local Brands Pitch Scripts

## Chapter purpose

This chapter gives field-ready local brand scripts.

---

## 10-second pitch

> The AI Plug helps local brands use AI to create better content, answer product questions, capture campaign interest, and follow up more consistently.

---

## 15-second pitch

> We help local brands figure out where AI can help first: product content, local visibility, customer questions, QR campaigns, events, promotions, follow-up, or internal support.

---

## 30-second pitch

> Most local brands do not need random AI tools. They need practical systems around how customers discover products, understand them, ask questions, scan QR codes, attend events, and follow up. We help find the first useful system and build from there.

---

## 60-second pitch

> Local brands need AI that supports their story, products, and customer interest without sounding generic. The first useful move may be better product content, local SEO, approved product FAQs, QR campaign paths, event interest capture, email/text follow-up, or internal content assistants. The AI Plug helps find the first practical AI use case, build it safely, and improve from there.

---

## Content pitch

> If content is the problem, AI can help you stop starting from zero every time you need a product post, caption, email, promo, landing page, or short-form video idea.

---

## Product question pitch

> If customers ask the same product questions repeatedly, an approved answer system can help. Not loose AI — approved product facts, clear boundaries, and staff handoff.

---

## QR campaign pitch

> QR codes should do more than send people to a generic homepage. They can capture product interest, event signups, promo opt-ins, waitlists, custom orders, or follow-up permission.

---

## Event/pop-up pitch

> Events and pop-ups create attention, but many brands lose the follow-up. AI and better intake can help capture interest and organize what happens after someone scans, signs up, or asks about a product.

---

## Internal assistant pitch

> The first AI system does not have to talk to customers. It can help you internally with product descriptions, captions, emails, customer replies, promo ideas, vendor outreach, and monthly recaps.

---

## Chapter 115 field script

> I would not sell you AI just because it is popular. I would look at your brand and ask where it could help first — content, product questions, QR campaigns, events, promotions, or follow-up.

Bridge question:

> If you could make one part of the brand easier or stronger first, what would it be?

---

## Chapter 115 training check

A rep passes this chapter if the pitch sounds specific to local brands.

A rep fails if the pitch sounds like generic social media management.

---

# Chapter 116 — Local Brands Outreach Scripts

## Chapter purpose

This chapter gives cold, warm, text, DM, email, phone, and follow-up scripts.

---

## Cold text

> Hey [Name], I help local brands figure out where AI can actually help — product content, customer questions, QR campaigns, event follow-up, promotions, and internal content support. Not sure if it is a fit, but are you looking at AI for the business yet?

---

## Short cold text

> Quick question — are you looking at ways AI could help with product content, customer questions, QR campaigns, or follow-up this year?

---

## Website-specific cold text

> Hey [Name], I looked at your site and had one thought: there may be an opportunity to make product questions, QR campaigns, promotions, or follow-up clearer with AI-supported systems. Would it be worth a quick look?

---

## Social-specific DM

> Hey [Name], I saw your brand page and wanted to reach out. I help local brands use AI in practical ways — product content, customer questions, QR campaigns, promo pages, event follow-up, and internal content support. Not a chatbot pitch. More about finding the first useful place AI can help.

---

## Event / pop-up DM

> Quick thought — if pop-ups, events, or markets matter for your brand, AI can help organize the QR path, capture interest, and create follow-up after people discover your products.

---

## Warm referral text

> [Referrer] mentioned you might be open to looking at AI for the business. I usually start by finding the first practical use case — content, product questions, QR campaigns, event follow-up, or internal assistant work. Want me to take a quick look?

---

## Cold email subject options

- Quick question about AI for [Brand Name]
- Is AI on your radar for product content?
- Practical AI for local brand content + QR campaigns
- Better product questions + follow-up
- Not a chatbot pitch — quick brand question

---

## Cold email

> Hi [Name],  
> I work with local brands and retail businesses on practical AI adoption — not hype, not staff replacement, and not random chatbots.  
>
> For local brands, the first useful AI move is usually one of these: stronger product content, approved product answers, QR campaign paths, event interest capture, promotion landing pages, or internal content support.  
>
> I wanted to ask: are you looking at where AI could help [Brand Name] this year, or is that still on the back burner?  
>
> — [Your Name]

---

## Call opener

> Hey [Name], this is [Your Name] with The AI Plug. I’ll keep it quick. I help local brands figure out where AI can practically help — product content, customer questions, QR campaigns, events, promotions, follow-up, and internal assistant work. I’m not calling to sell a random chatbot. Is AI something you’ve started thinking about for the business?

---

## Discovery bridge

> Before I recommend anything, can I ask how customers usually discover your products and what questions they ask before buying?

---

## After-conversation recap

> Hey [Name], good talking with you. Based on what you shared, I would not start with a giant AI build. The first useful move looks like [recommendation] because [reason]. That would help with [problem] while keeping [guardrail] clear.

---

## Proposal follow-up

> Hey [Name], just checking back on the proposal. I kept it focused on [first useful system], not everything at once. Do you want to review it, reduce scope, or pause for now?

---

## No-response follow-up

> Hey [Name], I do not want to keep bugging you. Should I keep this open, or would it be better to circle back later?

---

## Chapter 116 field script

> Outreach should connect to the brand’s actual world: products, content, events, QR campaigns, customer questions, and follow-up.

Bridge question:

> What specific observation can we make before reaching out?

---

## Chapter 116 training check

A rep passes this chapter if outreach feels specific and practical.

A rep fails if outreach sounds like generic AI spam.

---

# Chapter 117 — Local Brands Objection Handling

## Chapter purpose

This chapter gives objection responses for local brand and retail owners.

The structure:

1. Acknowledge.
2. Reframe.
3. Tie to the first useful system.
4. Avoid guarantees.
5. Offer a simple next step.

---

## Objection: “We already post on social.”

Response:

> That is good. The question is whether the content connects to product questions, search, QR campaigns, events, promotions, and follow-up. AI can help create a stronger system behind the posting.

Next step:

> We can review whether content consistency or the follow-up after attention is the first issue.

---

## Objection: “We already have a website.”

Response:

> That makes sense. Most businesses do. The question is whether the website helps customers understand products, ask questions, join campaigns, scan QR codes, or take the right next step.

Next step:

> We can review where the current site supports the product decision and where AI or better systems would help first.

---

## Objection: “I do not need AI.”

Response:

> That may be true. You may not need AI everywhere. The question is whether there is one place AI could help — content, product questions, QR campaigns, event follow-up, customer replies, or owner visibility. If there is not, we should not force it.

Next step:

> A review can tell us if there is a useful first move or not.

---

## Objection: “I do not want a chatbot.”

Response:

> I get that. A lot of chatbots are bad. We do not have to start with chat. AI might be more useful for content, product descriptions, customer reply drafts, QR campaign paths, promotion pages, or approved product FAQs.

Next step:

> Let’s find the best first use case before deciding on chat.

---

## Objection: “Can you guarantee sales?”

Response:

> No. Sales depend on demand, product fit, pricing, timing, reputation, and customer behavior. What we can do is improve content, product clarity, campaign paths, customer answers, and follow-up.

Next step:

> We can focus on what the brand can control.

---

## Objection: “I don’t want AI making false product claims.”

Response:

> That is the right concern. Product-facing AI should use approved facts, clear boundaries, and human handoff. In some cases, the better first move is internal content support before AI answers customers publicly.

Next step:

> Let’s identify what product facts are approved and what AI should never say.

---

## Objection: “We’re too small for this.”

Response:

> You may not need a full system. Smaller brands usually benefit from one practical AI use case first — content support, product FAQs, QR interest capture, email follow-up, or an internal assistant.

Next step:

> Let’s look at the smallest useful first move.

---

## Objection: “This sounds expensive.”

Response:

> I understand. That is why I would separate the full system from the first useful system. If the larger scope is too much, we can start with a review or one starter system and leave the rest for later.

Next step:

> Do you want me to price the smaller first step?

---

## Objection: “I can use ChatGPT myself.”

Response:

> You can, and you should. The difference is turning it into a business-specific system: your product facts, brand voice, approved claims, content templates, QR paths, customer replies, and follow-up process.

Next step:

> We can start by building the first business-specific content or product-answer system.

---

## Chapter 117 field script

> I hear you. The safe way to look at this is not “do you need AI everywhere?” It is “is there one place AI can help the brand create, answer, capture, or follow up better without making false claims?”

Bridge question:

> Would starting with a review or one smaller system make more sense?

---

## Chapter 117 training check

A rep passes this chapter if they handle objections without promising sales or making false product claims.

A rep fails if they push generic AI content after the owner expresses brand concern.

---

# Chapter 118 — Local Brands Pricing Logic

## Chapter purpose

This chapter translates the master pricing framework into Local Brands + Retail.

Pricing should reflect strategy, content volume, product-answer approval, QR/campaign complexity, follow-up, and ongoing support.

---

## Recommended offer ranges

### Local Brand AI Growth Review

Recommended setup:

**$497 – $1,500**

Best starting target:

**$750 – $1,000**

Use when the owner is unsure where AI fits.

Includes:
- brand/content review
- product question review
- QR/campaign review
- event/pop-up follow-up review
- internal assistant opportunity review
- first useful system recommendation

---

### AI Content + Social Media Engine

Recommended setup:

**$1,500 – $6,000+**

Monthly:

**$750 – $4,000+**

Use when product content, social rhythm, campaigns, launches, emails, captions, and short-form ideas are the main opportunity.

Price increases with:
- many platforms
- high post volume
- product count
- email/text content
- short-form video scripts
- graphics
- campaign volume
- scheduling/support

---

### SEO + AI Search Visibility

Recommended setup:

**$1,500 – $7,500+**

Monthly:

**$750 – $3,500+**

Use when local visibility, product/category pages, FAQ content, and AI search visibility matter.

Guardrail:
No ranking or sales guarantees.

---

### QR Campaign + Interest Capture System

Recommended setup:

**$750 – $5,000+**

Monthly:

**$250 – $1,500+**

Use when QR codes should capture product interest, event signups, waitlists, promotions, custom orders, or email/text permissions.

Price increases with:
- multiple QR paths
- event/campaign volume
- email/SMS capture
- follow-up automation
- landing page design
- source tracking
- dashboard integration

---

### Product Answer / AI Customer Experience Starter

Recommended setup:

**$2,500 – $10,000+**

Monthly:

**$500 – $2,500+**

Use when approved product answers, FAQ, website operator, or customer guidance is needed.

Price increases with:
- product count
- regulated claims
- availability/pricing boundaries
- many answer categories
- frequent updates
- handoff rules

---

### Paid Campaign + Landing Page System

Recommended setup:

**$1,500 – $7,500+**

Monthly management:

**$750 – $3,500+**

Ad spend:
Separate.

Use when the business has a clear product offer, promotion, launch, event, or seasonal campaign.

Guardrail:
No sales, revenue, traffic, or ad ROI guarantees.

---

### Internal AI Assistant Starter

Recommended setup:

**$1,500 – $10,000+**

Monthly:

**$500 – $3,000+**

Use when owner/staff repeat work can be supported internally.

Examples:
- content assistant
- product description assistant
- customer reply assistant
- promo planning assistant
- email assistant
- event recap assistant

---

### Full Local Brand AI Growth System

Recommended setup:

**$7,500 – $35,000+**

Monthly:

**$1,500 – $7,500+**

Use when multiple pieces need to connect:
- content
- local SEO
- product answers
- QR paths
- campaigns
- follow-up
- internal assistants
- owner visibility
- ongoing management

---

## Local brand pricing drivers

Price increases with:

- number of products/categories
- content volume
- campaign volume
- QR path complexity
- email/SMS integration
- product answer approval burden
- regulated product claims
- landing page count
- paid campaign support
- event/pop-up volume
- dashboard/source tracking
- monthly support

---

## Chapter 118 field script

> Pricing depends on whether we are doing a review, one starter system, or a full local brand AI growth system. Product content is different from QR campaigns, and both are different from product-answer systems or monthly content support.

Bridge question:

> Do you want the smallest useful first move priced, or the bigger system that could eventually connect everything?

---

## Chapter 118 training check

A rep passes this chapter if they explain price by scope and complexity.

A rep fails if they quote randomly without understanding product, content, and campaign needs.

---

# Chapter 119 — Local Brands Proposal + Handoff Templates

## Chapter purpose

This chapter gives proposal and internal handoff templates for local brands.

---

## Proposal structure

Every local brand proposal should include:

1. Brand summary
2. Problem diagnosed
3. Recommended first system
4. Why this comes first
5. Scope included
6. Scope excluded
7. Product/claim guardrails
8. Required approvals
9. Timeline estimate
10. Setup price
11. Monthly price if applicable
12. Pass-through costs
13. Next step

---

## Local Brand AI Growth Review proposal summary

> Based on our conversation, the safest first step is a Local Brand AI Growth Review. We will review how customers discover your products, what questions they ask, how content is created, whether QR/event/campaign paths capture interest, where follow-up is weak, and where AI could help first. The result is a recommendation for the first useful AI system, not a giant package by default.

---

## AI Content proposal summary

> We recommend starting with an AI Content + Social Media Engine because the main opportunity appears to be content and product storytelling. The system will help turn your products, story, customer questions, promotions, and events into stronger posts, pages, captions, emails, and campaign assets.

---

## Product Answer proposal summary

> We recommend starting with a Product Answer / AI Customer Experience Starter because customers ask repeat questions before buying. The system will create approved product answer language, boundaries, and handoff rules so customers can get clearer guidance without AI making false or unapproved claims.

---

## QR Campaign proposal summary

> We recommend starting with a QR Campaign + Interest Capture System because customers are showing interest through events, pop-ups, packaging, displays, or promotions, but that interest needs a clearer next step. The system can route scans to product pages, signups, waitlists, promotions, or follow-up paths.

---

## Internal AI Assistant proposal summary

> We recommend starting with an Internal AI Assistant because the owner/team repeats internal work that AI can help prepare. The assistant may support product descriptions, social captions, email drafts, customer replies, promo planning, vendor outreach, or monthly recaps while people remain in control.

---

## Full Local Brand AI Growth System proposal summary

> Your brand appears to have multiple connected opportunities: content, product answers, QR paths, campaigns, follow-up, internal work, and owner visibility. We recommend a phased Full Local Brand AI Growth System, beginning with the first useful system and expanding only where it makes business sense.

---

## Scope exclusions

Use these exclusions where relevant:

- no guaranteed sales
- no guaranteed traffic
- no guaranteed rankings
- no guaranteed revenue
- no guaranteed reviews
- no guaranteed social reach
- no guaranteed ad ROI
- no false product claims
- no health/safety/performance claims without approval
- no automatic customer-facing messages without approval
- no AI replacing staff
- ad spend separate
- third-party software separate

---

## Internal handoff template

Use after the sale or serious discovery call:

- Brand name:
- Contact:
- Product/category:
- Location / market:
- Current website:
- Current social links:
- Current sales channels:
- Main problem:
- Owner exact words:
- Recommended first system:
- Why this fits:
- What should wait:
- Product answer needs:
- Product claim guardrails:
- QR/campaign needs:
- Event/pop-up needs:
- Email/SMS follow-up needs:
- Staff/owner alerts:
- Current software:
- AI answer approval needs:
- Pricing discussed:
- Next action:
- Follow-up date:

---

## Chapter 119 field script

> I’ll write the proposal around the first useful system, not a vague AI package. It will say what problem we are solving, what is included, what is excluded, what product claims must be approved, and what the next step is.

Bridge question:

> Should I include the larger future phase as an option, or keep this focused only on the starter system?

---

## Chapter 119 training check

A rep passes this chapter if the proposal protects scope and product guardrails.

A rep fails if the proposal sounds like generic social media management.

---

# Chapter 120 — Local Brands Delivery + Launch SOP

## Chapter purpose

This chapter gives the delivery team the operational handoff needed to build safely.

---

## Intake checklist

Collect:

- brand name
- owner/contact
- phone/email
- website/social links
- product categories
- top products
- products to avoid
- sales channels
- locations/markets
- current content process
- current event/pop-up process
- current QR codes
- current email/SMS tools
- current forms
- staff roles
- routing destinations
- product answer needs
- product claim boundaries
- availability/pricing rules
- promotion rules
- approval contact
- public do-not-say list
- brand tone
- photo/video assets
- Google Business Profile link
- review/follow-up process

---

## Build checklist

Depending on scope:

### Content / campaign pages
- product copy
- category copy
- campaign pages
- promotion pages
- CTA buttons
- interest capture path
- mobile layout
- safe claims
- SEO metadata
- no false product claims

### QR / interest capture
- QR destination pages
- product interest form
- event signup
- waitlist
- promotion signup
- email/SMS capture
- source tracking if scoped
- confirmation message
- consent language
- internal alert

### AI Customer Experience
- approved product answer library
- FAQ categories
- do-not-say list
- handoff triggers
- product claim boundaries
- availability/pricing boundary language
- test questions
- fail-safe answer

### Internal assistant
- purpose
- knowledge base
- prompt rules
- templates
- output examples
- staff instructions
- approval rules
- update process

### Owner visibility
- product interest
- campaign source
- follow-up status
- customer questions
- notes
- monthly recap inputs
- next recommended improvement

---

## Launch QA checklist

Before launch:

- test mobile layout
- test desktop layout
- test all buttons
- test forms
- test QR paths
- test email/SMS capture if included
- test alerts
- test confirmation message
- test dashboard entry if included
- test AI answers with approved questions
- test AI refusal/handoff for unsafe product claims
- confirm no guarantees appear publicly
- confirm phone/email/location are correct
- confirm product claims are approved
- confirm no automatic public messages without approval

---

## Post-launch check

Within the first week:

- confirm signups/interest capture are received
- confirm alerts work
- confirm owner/staff knows what to do
- confirm owner can see what matters
- collect feedback
- identify confusing fields
- note repeated questions
- note follow-up issues
- recommend next improvement

---

## Chapter 120 field script

> The build is not done when the page or QR code looks good. It is done when product claims, interest capture, alerts, approvals, AI boundaries, and follow-up have been tested.

Bridge question:

> Who needs to approve product claims before anything goes live?

---

## Chapter 120 training check

A rep passes this chapter if they understand product claim safety and approval.

A rep fails if they treat launch as only publishing a page or QR code.

---

# Chapter 122 — Local Brands Monthly Recap + Renewal Logic

## Chapter purpose

This chapter teaches how to keep value visible after launch.

Monthly support should not be vague.

It should show what was reviewed, updated, improved, and recommended next.

---

## Monthly recap sections

A local brand monthly recap can include:

1. What was updated
2. Product interest reviewed
3. Common customer questions
4. QR/campaign notes
5. Event/pop-up follow-up notes
6. Content opportunities
7. Product answer updates needed
8. Internal assistant improvements
9. Owner visibility notes
10. Recommended next improvement

---

## Monthly recap example

> This month we reviewed product questions, QR campaign activity, and content needs. The biggest pattern is that customers are asking about [topic] before taking action. We recommend adding approved answer language for that question and creating a QR/campaign path for [product/promo/event]. No sales, traffic, rankings, or revenue are guaranteed, but this should make the next step clearer for customers and the brand.

---

## Renewal triggers

Renewal or upsell may make sense when:

- new product pages are needed
- content rhythm needs support
- QR paths should be added
- FAQ library needs expansion
- event/pop-up follow-up needs improvement
- email/SMS campaigns are needed
- paid social needs landing pages
- owner wants better product-interest visibility
- product launch campaign is coming
- seasonal campaign is coming
- customer reply assistant needs more templates

---

## Renewal script

> The first system is live. The next question is whether we keep it as-is or improve the next bottleneck. Based on what we saw, the best next improvement is probably [recommendation].

---

## Upsell script

> This is not about adding random features. The next improvement connects to what showed up after launch: [product question / QR path issue / follow-up issue / content opportunity / campaign need].

---

## Chapter 122 field script

> Monthly support should answer: what changed, what did we learn, what needs attention, and what is the next practical AI opportunity?

Bridge question:

> What did the first system reveal that we should improve next?

---

## Chapter 122 training check

A rep passes this chapter if they can explain monthly value without vague retainer language.

A rep fails if monthly support sounds like maintenance only.

---

# Chapter 123 — Local Brands Certification Test

## Chapter purpose

This chapter provides a test to certify reps for the Local Brands + Retail vertical.

---

## Section 1 — Multiple choice

### 1. What is the best first step for a local brand owner who is interested in AI but does not know where to start?

A. Full AI Growth System  
B. Local Brand AI Growth Review  
C. Public chatbot immediately  
D. Generic website redesign only  

Correct answer: **B**

---

### 2. A boutique struggles with product posts, style captions, and seasonal drops. Best first move?

A. AI Content + Social Engine  
B. Guaranteed sales campaign  
C. Transportation request form  
D. AI replacement salesperson  

Correct answer: **A**

---

### 3. A pop-up vendor gets QR scans but no follow-up. Best first move?

A. QR Interest Capture + Follow-Up Workflow  
B. Generic blog package  
C. Public AI chatbot for everything  
D. Guaranteed conversion campaign  

Correct answer: **A**

---

### 4. A local brand says AI might make false product claims. Best answer?

A. AI can say anything if prompted  
B. Product-facing AI should use approved facts, claim boundaries, and human handoff  
C. Claims do not matter  
D. AI should replace staff answers  

Correct answer: **B**

---

### 5. A retail shop wants more local discovery. Best first move?

A. Local SEO + AI Search Visibility  
B. AI dispatch system  
C. Restaurant Partner Program  
D. Guaranteed revenue funnel  

Correct answer: **A**

---

## Section 2 — Short answer

### Prompt 1

Explain The AI Plug to a local brand owner without AI hype.

Strong answer should include:

- practical AI adoption
- content, product answers, QR campaigns, event follow-up, internal support, or local visibility
- approved product facts
- safe first system
- no guarantees

---

### Prompt 2

Explain why social posting alone may not solve the problem.

Strong answer:

> Social can create attention, but the business can still lose opportunities if product questions, QR paths, event follow-up, email/text capture, and customer replies are not handled clearly after someone shows interest.

---

### Prompt 3

Write a safe response to “Can you guarantee sales?”

Strong answer:

> No. Sales depend on demand, product fit, pricing, timing, reputation, and customer behavior. What we can do is improve content, product clarity, campaign paths, customer answers, and follow-up.

---

### Prompt 4

Name three AI Business Assistant uses for local brands.

Strong answers:

- product description assistant
- social caption assistant
- email campaign assistant
- customer reply assistant
- promo planning assistant
- event recap assistant
- vendor outreach assistant

---

### Prompt 5

Name three things AI should not promise in local brands/retail.

Strong answers:

- guaranteed sales
- guaranteed traffic
- guaranteed rankings
- guaranteed revenue
- guaranteed social reach
- false product claims
- health/safety claims without approval
- exact availability unless approved
- staff replacement

---

## Section 3 — Scenario

### Scenario

A local product brand sells at pop-ups. People scan QR codes, ask product questions, and say they are interested, but the owner does not capture email/text follow-up or product preferences.

### Required answer

Recommend the first useful AI system and explain why.

Strong answer:

> I would recommend a QR Interest Capture + Follow-Up Workflow. The system should route scans to product interest, email/text permission, product preferences, and follow-up prompts. It should use approved product facts and avoid false claims. I would not promise sales, scan volume, traffic, or revenue.

---

## Section 4 — Roleplay

### Roleplay objection

Owner says:

> “I don’t want AI making my brand sound generic.”

Strong answer:

> That is a real concern. The goal is not generic AI content. The system should use your product facts, tone, story, approved claims, and examples so AI supports your brand instead of flattening it.

---

## Final pass standard

A rep passes this vertical if they can:

- speak in product/brand/campaign/event language
- diagnose the first useful system
- avoid guarantees
- explain AI advantage without hype
- recommend safe first steps
- switch language by retail/brand type
- write clean proposal summaries
- hand off delivery details clearly
- explain monthly support as ongoing improvement

A rep fails if they:

- promise sales, traffic, revenue, rankings, reviews, or social reach
- lead with generic AI tools
- push chatbots too early
- ignore product claim guardrails
- recommend a full system before diagnosis
- cannot explain the difference between content, product answers, QR paths, campaigns, internal assistants, and owner visibility

---

# Part 12 quality-control checklist

Before this section is approved, confirm:

- It follows AI Advantage First.
- It speaks to local brand and retail owner reality.
- It prioritizes product storytelling, content, product answers, QR paths, events, follow-up, and owner visibility.
- It translates AI into marketing, customer response, intake, internal assistants, owner visibility, and ongoing adaptation.
- It includes discovery, scripts, objections, pricing, proposals, delivery, QA, monthly recaps, local brand modules, and certification.
- It avoids guarantees.
- It avoids unsafe product-claim language.
- It is dashboard-ready.
- It can be merged into the complete master manual later.

---

# The AI Plug Master Manual v3 — Part 13: Dashboard Lead Classification + Handoff
**AI Advantage First operating system section**  
**Date:** 2026-05-27  
**Project:** Where To Go SA / The AI Plug  
**Public visitor brand:** Where To Go SA  
**Business systems brand:** The AI Plug  
**Manual type:** Full-depth operations and dashboard training manual  
**Section covered:** Part 13 — Dashboard Lead Classification + Handoff

---

## Upload note

Do **not** upload this file into the ChatGPT Project folder yet unless space is available and dashboard work is being actively updated.

This is a working manual part. After all manual parts are complete, this section should be merged into:

`THE_AI_PLUG_MASTER_MANUAL_V3_COMPLETE_2026-05-27.md`

---

## Direction lock for this section

This section follows the corrected AI Advantage First direction.

The dashboard should not classify every business lead as:

- website lead
- form lead
- chatbot lead
- dashboard lead
- lead path lead
- simple marketing lead

That old direction is too narrow.

The dashboard should classify leads around the real AI Plug offer system:

# AI advantage first. Practical first AI move. Service lane. Vertical fit. Guardrails. Next action.

The dashboard should help answer:

1. What type of business is this?
2. What is the owner’s real problem?
3. What AI advantage lane fits first?
4. What should be recommended first?
5. What should not be promised?
6. What needs approval?
7. What should sales do next?
8. What should delivery know before building?

The dashboard is not just a storage place for leads.

It is a decision-support system for selling and delivering The AI Plug correctly.

---

# Chapter 124 — Dashboard Purpose

## Chapter purpose

This chapter defines what the AI Plug dashboard should do after the business direction changed.

The dashboard should help The AI Plug operate like a real AI adoption and growth systems company.

It should support:

- lead intake
- business type classification
- service lane classification
- first useful system recommendation
- sales follow-up
- proposal creation
- guardrail awareness
- delivery handoff
- monthly recap
- renewal and upsell logic
- vertical training support

It should not turn The AI Plug into a generic lead database.

---

## The dashboard’s real job

The dashboard’s real job is to make sure the next person knows:

- what the prospect said
- what the prospect actually needs
- what service lane fits
- what vertical language should be used
- what should be sold first
- what should wait
- what must not be promised
- what must be approved before launch
- what follow-up should happen next

A good dashboard protects the company from selling the wrong thing.

---

## The old dashboard risk

The old dashboard direction could accidentally push everything into:

- lead path
- website
- forms
- routing
- follow-up
- restaurant leads only
- static sales notes

Those are still useful pieces, but they are not the whole business.

The new dashboard must support the broader offer:

- AI Growth Review
- AI Marketing Systems
- AI Customer Experience
- AI Intake + Automation
- AI Business Assistants
- AI Growth Management
- Full AI Growth System

---

## Dashboard success standard

The dashboard is successful if a rep can open a lead and quickly understand:

- “This is a home services lead.”
- “The owner is worried about quote requests and follow-up.”
- “The first useful system is probably Smart Intake + Automation.”
- “Do not promise jobs or leads.”
- “Need photo upload and service-area fields.”
- “Next step: AI Growth Review or starter proposal.”
- “Delivery needs approved customer language before launch.”

That is the level of clarity required.

---

## Chapter 124 field script

Use this when explaining the dashboard internally:

> The dashboard is not just where we store leads. It helps us classify the business, identify the first useful AI move, protect the guardrails, and hand the opportunity from sales to delivery without losing context.

Bridge question:

> What should the next person know so they do not sell or build the wrong thing?

---

## Chapter 124 training check

A team member passes this chapter if they understand the dashboard as decision support.

They fail if they treat it as a generic contact list.

---

# Chapter 125 — Core Lead Classification Fields

## Chapter purpose

This chapter defines the core fields every AI Plug lead should have.

These fields should support selling, quoting, delivery, and follow-up.

---

## Required lead fields

Every AI Plug lead should capture:

- Lead name
- Business name
- Contact name
- Phone
- Email
- Website
- Social links
- Source
- Date received
- Business type
- Service lane
- Starting point
- Problem type
- Owner’s exact words
- AI awareness level
- Urgency
- Budget signal
- Guardrail risk
- Recommended first step
- Proposal status
- Follow-up status
- Next action
- Notes

---

## Business type field

Use these options:

- Home Services + Contractors
- Hospitality + Local Experience
- Restaurants
- Professional Services
- Transportation + Concierge
- Local Brands + Retail
- Other / Custom

If the business fits multiple types, choose the primary buyer context.

Example:

A restaurant is technically hospitality, but if it came through the restaurant funnel, classify it as:

**Restaurants**

A black car company offering visitor plans should be:

**Transportation + Concierge**

A boutique that runs pop-ups should be:

**Local Brands + Retail**

---

## Service lane field

Use these options:

- AI Growth Review
- AI Marketing Systems
- AI Customer Experience
- AI Intake + Automation
- AI Business Assistants
- AI Growth Management
- Full AI Growth System
- Restaurant Partner Program / Visitor Visibility
- Other / Custom

This should represent the main recommended lane, not every possible future lane.

---

## Starting point field

Use these options:

- AI Website + Conversion System
- AI Content + Social Media Engine
- SEO + AI Search Visibility
- Paid Campaign + Landing Page System
- AI Chat Operator / Customer Experience
- AI Phone / Voice Planning
- Smart Intake + Automation
- Internal AI Assistants + Workflow Support
- QR Campaign / Menu Path
- Visitor Visibility Review
- Provider Handoff Workflow
- Consultation Intake + Qualification
- Product Answer / Customer Experience
- Other / Custom

This field should describe the most practical first build or review.

---

## Problem type field

Use these options:

- AI unclear / needs review
- marketing output weak
- search visibility weak
- repeated customer questions
- intake/request details messy
- follow-up inconsistent
- staff/owner busywork
- internal assistant opportunity
- owner visibility weak
- paid campaign readiness
- voice/phone planning
- private event/catering/group inquiries
- consultation qualification
- product questions
- QR/event interest capture
- transportation provider handoff
- multiple connected needs
- other / custom

---

## AI awareness level

Use these options:

- Unaware
- Curious but unclear
- Has tried basic AI
- Actively exploring AI
- Ready to build
- Already using AI but needs structure
- Skeptical / cautious

This helps determine whether the next step is education, review, or proposal.

---

## Guardrail risk

Use these options:

- Low
- Medium
- High

High-risk examples:

- professional advice
- legal / medical / tax / financial / insurance boundaries
- safety-sensitive trade claims
- transportation availability
- emergency response
- customer-facing AI without approved answers
- regulated product claims
- unapproved pricing / availability
- paid campaign guarantees

---

## Chapter 125 field script

Use this when entering a lead:

> We need to classify the lead by business type, service lane, starting point, problem type, AI awareness, guardrail risk, and next action. If those are missing, the next person will not know what to do.

Bridge question:

> What is the real first useful AI move for this lead?

---

## Chapter 125 training check

A team member passes this chapter if they can classify a lead without forcing it into the wrong service lane.

They fail if every lead becomes “website” or “chatbot.”

---

# Chapter 126 — Business Type Classification Guide

## Chapter purpose

This chapter teaches how to choose the correct business type.

Business type matters because the sales language, guardrails, and first useful system change by vertical.

---

## Home Services + Contractors

Use for:

- roofing
- flooring
- HVAC
- plumbing
- electrical
- remodeling
- restoration
- landscaping
- cleaning
- handyman
- local service contractors

Common first systems:

- Smart Intake + Automation
- AI Marketing Systems
- SEO + AI Search Visibility
- AI Customer Experience
- Internal AI Assistants
- Full Home Services AI Growth System

Common guardrails:

- no guaranteed jobs
- no emergency response promises
- no diagnosis
- no insurance claim approval promises
- no financing/warranty claims without approval

---

## Hospitality + Local Experience

Use for:

- bars
- rooftops
- venues
- attractions
- tours
- local experiences
- resort-area businesses
- visitor-facing businesses not strictly restaurants

Common first systems:

- AI Marketing Systems
- AI Customer Experience
- Event / Group Intake
- QR Campaign Path
- Internal AI Assistants
- Full Hospitality AI Growth System

Common guardrails:

- no guaranteed traffic
- no guaranteed bookings
- no guaranteed event attendance
- no unapproved public answers

---

## Restaurants

Use for:

- restaurants
- dining groups
- bars/restaurants when restaurant offer is primary
- private dining
- catering restaurants
- group dining restaurants

Common first systems:

- Restaurant Partner Program / Visitor Visibility
- AI Restaurant Growth Review
- Private Event / Catering Intake
- AI Content + Social Media Engine
- QR + Menu Path
- AI Customer Experience
- Full AI Restaurant Growth System

Common guardrails:

- no guaranteed reservations
- no guaranteed visitor traffic
- no guaranteed placement
- no guaranteed event bookings
- no unapproved menu/allergy answers

---

## Professional Services

Use for:

- attorneys
- consultants
- insurance agencies
- accounting/tax/bookkeeping
- medical/wellness practices
- real estate
- financial-style services
- recruiting/staffing
- B2B advisors

Common first systems:

- Professional Services AI Growth Review
- Authority Content + SEO
- Consultation Intake + Qualification
- Approved Process FAQs
- Internal AI Assistants
- Full Professional Services AI Growth System

Common guardrails:

- no professional advice by AI
- no legal/medical/tax/financial/insurance advice
- no guaranteed clients
- no guaranteed outcomes
- approval required for customer-facing language

---

## Transportation + Concierge

Use for:

- transportation providers
- black car
- shuttles
- airport/resort transfers
- concierge request systems
- group transportation
- tour/transport businesses

Common first systems:

- Transportation AI Growth Review
- Route Visibility / SEO
- Transportation Request Intake
- Provider Handoff Workflow
- AI Phone / Voice Planning
- AI Customer Experience

Common guardrails:

- no guaranteed pickup
- no guaranteed availability
- no exact drive times
- no provider confirmation without provider approval
- no illegal/unlicensed service implication

---

## Local Brands + Retail

Use for:

- boutiques
- retail shops
- makers
- local product brands
- pop-ups
- gift brands
- specialty product brands
- local e-commerce/pickup brands

Common first systems:

- Local Brand AI Growth Review
- AI Content + Social Media Engine
- Product Answer / AI Customer Experience
- QR Campaign + Interest Capture
- SEO + AI Search Visibility
- Internal AI Assistants

Common guardrails:

- no guaranteed sales
- no false product claims
- no unapproved health/safety claims
- no guaranteed traffic/rankings/social reach

---

## Other / Custom

Use when:

- the lead does not fit a main vertical
- the business is unusual
- multiple verticals are equally strong
- a custom manual or playbook is needed

In this case, use the Universal Vertical Translation Template.

---

## Chapter 126 field script

> The business type determines how we talk, what we recommend first, and what we must not promise. Choose the business type based on how the owner buys and what the customer needs, not just the industry label.

Bridge question:

> Which vertical language would make this owner feel understood fastest?

---

## Chapter 126 training check

A team member passes this chapter if they can choose the correct vertical and explain why.

They fail if they use the same pitch for every business.

---

# Chapter 127 — Service Lane Recommendation Logic

## Chapter purpose

This chapter teaches how to pick the right service lane.

The service lane should match the owner’s real problem.

---

## AI Growth Review

Recommend when:

- owner is curious but unclear
- multiple problems exist
- rep lacks enough detail
- guardrails need review
- owner needs safe first step
- business has risk or complexity

Dashboard clue phrases:

- “I know I need AI but don’t know where.”
- “What can AI do for us?”
- “We need to figure this out.”
- “I don’t know where to start.”
- “We need a roadmap.”

Next action:

- schedule review
- collect website/social/tools
- prepare discovery questions

---

## AI Marketing Systems

Recommend when:

- content is weak
- search visibility is weak
- pages are weak
- social rhythm is weak
- paid campaigns need landing pages
- business needs better authority/visibility

Dashboard clue phrases:

- “We need better marketing.”
- “We don’t post enough.”
- “We need SEO.”
- “People don’t know about us.”
- “Our competitors look more active.”
- “We need ads but don’t know where to send them.”

Next action:

- review website/content/social
- identify content pillars
- recommend content/search/campaign scope

---

## AI Customer Experience

Recommend when:

- customer questions repeat
- website does not guide decisions
- owner wants chat/operator carefully
- approved answer library is needed
- voice planning may matter

Dashboard clue phrases:

- “Customers ask the same questions.”
- “Staff repeats answers.”
- “People don’t know what to do next.”
- “We need a chatbot but I’m worried.”
- “I don’t want AI saying the wrong thing.”

Next action:

- collect common questions
- define safe answers
- define handoff rules

---

## AI Intake + Automation

Recommend when:

- request details are messy
- forms are weak
- follow-up is inconsistent
- routing is unclear
- photos/documents/details are missing
- multiple inquiry channels exist

Dashboard clue phrases:

- “We need better forms.”
- “People don’t send enough info.”
- “Requests come from everywhere.”
- “Nobody knows who followed up.”
- “We need alerts.”
- “We need routing.”

Next action:

- map request types
- define required fields
- define routing/alerts
- define confirmation and follow-up

---

## AI Business Assistants

Recommend when:

- owner/staff repeat internal work
- drafts, summaries, proposals, content, research, SOPs are needed
- public AI feels risky
- team needs support before customer-facing AI

Dashboard clue phrases:

- “I write the same things over and over.”
- “Staff needs scripts.”
- “We need proposal help.”
- “Content takes too long.”
- “I need summaries.”
- “We don’t want AI talking to customers yet.”

Next action:

- choose one assistant use case
- collect knowledge base
- define output templates
- define approval process

---

## AI Growth Management

Recommend when:

- system needs ongoing updates
- content rhythm needed
- answer library needs updating
- campaigns need monthly support
- owner wants ongoing AI adaptation
- multiple systems are active

Dashboard clue phrases:

- “Who keeps this updated?”
- “We need monthly content.”
- “AI keeps changing.”
- “We need ongoing help.”
- “We don’t want this to go stale.”

Next action:

- define monthly scope
- define recap format
- define update cadence

---

## Full AI Growth System

Recommend when:

- multiple problems are connected
- business has budget and readiness
- marketing, intake, answers, internal work, and follow-up all matter
- owner wants ongoing support
- phased build makes sense

Dashboard clue phrases:

- “Everything is disconnected.”
- “We need marketing, follow-up, forms, and AI.”
- “We want the full system.”
- “We need ongoing help.”
- “We’re ready to build this right.”

Next action:

- phase the scope
- start with review or phase one
- avoid promising outcomes

---

## Chapter 127 field script

> The service lane should come from the owner’s problem, not from what we want to sell. If the owner is unclear, recommend review. If one problem is obvious, recommend the first useful system. If multiple pieces are connected, phase the full system.

Bridge question:

> What did the owner say that tells us which lane fits first?

---

## Chapter 127 training check

A team member passes this chapter if they can justify the lane using the owner’s words.

They fail if they recommend the full system without diagnosis.

---

# Chapter 128 — Guardrail Tagging + Safe Claims

## Chapter purpose

This chapter teaches how to tag risk and protect the company from bad promises.

Every lead should have guardrail awareness.

---

## Universal do-not-promise list

Never promise:

- guaranteed leads
- guaranteed traffic
- guaranteed rankings
- guaranteed revenue
- guaranteed bookings
- guaranteed reservations
- guaranteed appointments
- guaranteed jobs
- guaranteed reviews
- guaranteed social reach
- guaranteed ad ROI
- guaranteed QR scans
- guaranteed event turnout
- guaranteed client outcomes
- staff replacement
- unsupervised public AI
- professional advice
- legal/tax/medical/financial/insurance advice
- automatic customer messages without approval

---

## Low risk

Examples:

- internal content assistant
- social caption drafts
- general business review
- non-public internal summaries
- basic website copy without sensitive claims
- product descriptions with approved facts

Dashboard action:

- normal sales process
- still require approval for public content

---

## Medium risk

Examples:

- customer-facing FAQ
- smart intake with customer confirmation
- paid campaign landing pages
- claims about service process
- QR paths
- event inquiries
- pricing range language
- follow-up drafts

Dashboard action:

- require approved language
- identify do-not-say list
- confirm human handoff

---

## High risk

Examples:

- legal/medical/tax/financial/insurance boundaries
- transportation availability
- emergency service claims
- safety-sensitive trade questions
- health/supplement/product claims
- AI phone/voice flows
- public AI answers without clear approvals
- pricing/availability promises
- regulated industries

Dashboard action:

- flag high risk
- require approval before proposal or build
- recommend review first if unclear
- document do-not-say list
- use human handoff
- avoid public AI until boundaries are clear

---

## Vertical-specific guardrail examples

### Home Services

Flag when:

- emergency response
- electrical/plumbing/HVAC safety
- insurance claims
- financing
- warranty promises
- diagnosis

Safe line:

> AI can collect details and explain process, but judgment and promises stay with the business.

---

### Restaurants / Hospitality

Flag when:

- reservations
- availability
- allergen/menu details
- alcohol/age policies
- event booking guarantees
- visitor traffic claims

Safe line:

> AI can support approved answers and inquiry collection, but it should not promise availability, reservations, or traffic.

---

### Professional Services

Flag when:

- legal advice
- medical advice
- tax advice
- financial advice
- insurance advice
- case/project outcomes

Safe line:

> AI can support process, intake, drafts, and internal prep, but professional judgment stays human.

---

### Transportation

Flag when:

- guaranteed pickup
- exact drive time
- provider availability
- licensed service
- emergency transportation
- dispatch

Safe line:

> AI can collect request details and prepare handoff, but confirmation stays with the right person or provider.

---

### Local Brands

Flag when:

- health claims
- safety claims
- product performance
- regulated products
- false availability
- fake scarcity

Safe line:

> AI can use approved product facts, but it should not invent claims.

---

## Chapter 128 field script

> Before we build or pitch anything customer-facing, we need to know what AI must not say. The dashboard should flag risk early so sales, proposal, and delivery stay safe.

Bridge question:

> What promise, claim, or answer would create risk if AI said it wrong?

---

## Chapter 128 training check

A team member passes this chapter if they tag risk before proposal/build.

They fail if they treat all AI answers as low-risk.

---

# Chapter 129 — Sales-to-Proposal Handoff

## Chapter purpose

This chapter teaches how to hand a lead from sales conversation to proposal writing.

A proposal should not be written from vague notes.

It should be written from a clear handoff.

---

## Required handoff sections

Every proposal handoff should include:

1. Business summary
2. Owner’s exact words
3. Problem diagnosed
4. Recommended first system
5. Why this comes first
6. What should wait
7. Scope suggested
8. Guardrails
9. Approval needs
10. Pricing direction
11. Next step

---

## Proposal handoff template

Use this:

- Business name:
- Contact:
- Business type:
- Lead source:
- Owner’s exact words:
- Main problem:
- Recommended service lane:
- Recommended starting point:
- Why this first:
- What should wait:
- Suggested scope:
- Exclusions / no guarantees:
- Guardrail risk:
- Approval needed:
- Pricing range discussed:
- Recommended proposal type:
- Next action:
- Follow-up date:

---

## What “owner’s exact words” means

Do not sanitize everything into agency language.

If the owner said:

> “People DM us and then nobody follows up.”

Keep that.

If the owner said:

> “I don’t want AI promising rides.”

Keep that.

If the owner said:

> “I’m tired of writing the same reply.”

Keep that.

The owner’s words help the proposal sound real.

---

## Proposal type options

Use:

- AI Growth Review Proposal
- Starter System Proposal
- Full AI Growth System Proposal
- Monthly AI Growth Management Proposal
- Restaurant Partner / Visibility Review Proposal
- Hybrid Proposal

Hybrid means more than one lane is included but still phased.

---

## What should wait

Every handoff should list what should wait.

Examples:

- public AI operator should wait until answers are approved
- paid ads should wait until landing page is ready
- full system should wait until review is done
- voice agent should wait until call rules are mapped
- dashboard should wait until workflow is clear
- monthly content should wait until brand voice is approved

This builds trust and prevents overbuilding.

---

## Chapter 129 field script

> The proposal should be written from what the owner actually said. We need the problem, first useful system, why it comes first, what should wait, guardrails, and next step.

Bridge question:

> What did the owner say that should appear in the proposal?

---

## Chapter 129 training check

A team member passes this chapter if the proposal handoff is specific enough to write without guessing.

They fail if the handoff says only “client interested in AI.”

---

# Chapter 130 — Sales-to-Delivery Handoff

## Chapter purpose

This chapter teaches how to hand an approved project to delivery.

Delivery should not have to reverse-engineer the sale.

The handoff must protect scope, approvals, and guardrails.

---

## Required delivery handoff sections

Every delivery handoff should include:

1. Approved offer
2. Approved scope
3. Business type
4. Service lane
5. Starting point
6. What is excluded
7. Required assets
8. Required approvals
9. Guardrails
10. Test plan
11. Launch conditions
12. Monthly support plan if included

---

## Delivery handoff template

Use this:

- Business name:
- Contact:
- Approved offer:
- Setup price:
- Monthly price:
- Business type:
- Service lane:
- Starting point:
- Problem being solved:
- Approved scope:
- Excluded scope:
- Required assets:
- Required access:
- Required approvals:
- AI answer boundaries:
- Do-not-say list:
- Forms/intake fields:
- Routing/alert rules:
- Dashboard/source tags:
- Launch QA required:
- Monthly support included:
- First post-launch review date:

---

## Delivery must know exclusions

If the client did not buy:

- ads
- SEO
- custom dashboard
- voice agent
- full website
- monthly content
- CRM integration
- public AI chat
- SMS automation
- image/video production

Then delivery must know that.

Do not let vague sales language expand scope accidentally.

---

## Delivery must know approvals

Delivery must know who approves:

- website copy
- service descriptions
- product claims
- AI answers
- pricing language
- availability language
- menu/allergen language
- professional boundaries
- transportation confirmation rules
- form fields
- automation messages
- launch

No customer-facing AI should go live without approved language.

---

## Delivery must know test plan

Every delivery handoff should include what must be tested:

- mobile layout
- buttons
- forms
- QR paths
- alerts
- routing
- confirmation message
- dashboard entry
- AI answers
- AI refusal/handoff
- guardrail questions
- owner/staff handoff
- post-launch feedback loop

---

## Chapter 130 field script

> Delivery needs more than “build the system.” They need scope, exclusions, approvals, guardrails, fields, routing, and launch tests. Otherwise the build can drift or create risk.

Bridge question:

> What does delivery need to know before touching this project?

---

## Chapter 130 training check

A team member passes this chapter if delivery could build from the handoff without guessing.

They fail if delivery has to ask basic scope questions after approval.

---

# Chapter 131 — Follow-Up Status + Pipeline Management

## Chapter purpose

This chapter teaches how to manage lead stages and follow-up inside the dashboard.

The goal is to prevent leads from disappearing.

---

## Recommended lead stages

Use these statuses:

- New Lead
- Needs Review
- Discovery Scheduled
- Discovery Completed
- Review Recommended
- Proposal Needed
- Proposal Sent
- Follow-Up Due
- Scope Revision Needed
- Won / Deposit Paid
- In Delivery
- Launched
- Monthly Management
- Not Now
- Not Fit
- Lost

---

## Follow-up fields

Every lead should include:

- Last contact date
- Next follow-up date
- Follow-up type
- Follow-up message needed
- Objection / concern
- Decision maker
- Proposal link/status
- Next action

---

## Follow-up type options

Use:

- send recap
- schedule discovery
- send review scope
- send proposal
- revise scope
- price follow-up
- answer objection
- check decision
- collect assets
- collect approval
- post-launch check
- monthly recap

---

## Not Now status

Use Not Now when:

- prospect is interested but not ready
- budget timing is wrong
- owner wants to revisit later
- needs internal discussion
- not urgent

Not Now should include:

- reason
- revisit date
- likely first offer later
- follow-up note

---

## Not Fit status

Use Not Fit when:

- prospect wants guarantees
- prospect expects AI to replace staff
- prospect wants unsafe automation
- prospect has no budget and no review interest
- prospect wants illegal/unethical claims
- scope is outside The AI Plug
- owner refuses approvals for customer-facing AI

Not Fit should include:

- reason
- safe final message
- no hard feelings

---

## Lost status

Use Lost when:

- prospect chose another provider
- prospect declined
- prospect stopped responding after follow-up
- offer no longer relevant

Lost should include:

- reason if known
- what we learned
- possible future reactivation

---

## Chapter 131 field script

> Every lead needs a next action or a clear reason it is paused, lost, or not fit. If there is no next action, the dashboard is not doing its job.

Bridge question:

> What is the next clear action for this lead?

---

## Chapter 131 training check

A team member passes this chapter if no active lead sits without a next action.

They fail if leads pile up with vague statuses.

---

# Chapter 132 — Monthly Recap + Renewal Dashboard Logic

## Chapter purpose

This chapter teaches how the dashboard should support monthly management and renewals.

Monthly AI Growth Management should not be vague.

The dashboard should help produce clear recaps.

---

## Monthly recap fields

For active monthly clients, capture:

- Client name
- Business type
- Active service lanes
- Month reviewed
- What was updated
- What was reviewed
- Common questions observed
- Workflow issues observed
- Content opportunities
- AI answer updates needed
- Follow-up issues
- Owner visibility notes
- Recommended next improvement
- Upsell/renewal opportunity
- Approval needed
- Next month focus

---

## Monthly recap output

A strong recap says:

1. What was done.
2. What was noticed.
3. What needs attention.
4. What is recommended next.
5. What is not guaranteed.
6. What needs approval.

Example:

> This month we reviewed the inquiry path, customer questions, and content needs. The biggest pattern is that customers are asking about [topic]. We recommend adding approved answer language and updating the intake form to collect [field]. No results are guaranteed, but this should make the next step clearer for customers and staff.

---

## Renewal opportunity triggers

Flag renewal or upsell when:

- new content needed
- answer library needs expansion
- new service/location/product added
- intake form needs improvement
- follow-up workflow needs refinement
- monthly content requested
- paid campaign readiness appears
- voice planning becomes relevant
- internal assistant should expand
- dashboard/owner visibility needed
- client asks about “what else can AI do?”

---

## What not to do

Do not turn monthly recap into:

- vanity report only
- raw analytics dump
- vague “maintenance”
- guaranteed results recap
- upsell spam
- generic AI trend list

It should connect to the client’s system and next practical improvement.

---

## Chapter 132 field script

> Monthly support should answer what changed, what we noticed, what needs approval, and what practical AI improvement should happen next.

Bridge question:

> What did this month reveal that we should improve?

---

## Chapter 132 training check

A team member passes this chapter if monthly recaps are specific and useful.

They fail if monthly support sounds like vague maintenance.

---

# Chapter 133 — Dashboard QA Checklist

## Chapter purpose

This chapter provides a checklist for whether the dashboard supports the corrected direction.

---

## Required dashboard QA

Check that the dashboard has fields for:

- Business type
- Service lane
- Starting point
- Problem type
- AI awareness level
- Guardrail risk
- Owner’s exact words
- Recommended first step
- What should wait
- Approval needs
- Safe claims
- Pricing direction
- Proposal status
- Follow-up status
- Next action
- Delivery handoff notes
- Monthly recap notes

---

## Direction QA

Confirm the dashboard does not force every lead into:

- website
- lead path
- form
- chatbot
- dashboard
- SEO
- ads

Those can be starting points, but the dashboard must also support:

- AI Growth Review
- AI Marketing Systems
- AI Customer Experience
- AI Intake + Automation
- AI Business Assistants
- AI Growth Management
- Full AI Growth System
- Restaurant Partner Program / Visitor Visibility
- vertical-specific offers

---

## Guardrail QA

Confirm every customer-facing AI lead has:

- approved answer need
- do-not-say list
- human handoff requirement
- risk tag
- approval contact
- launch QA requirement

---

## Follow-up QA

Confirm every active lead has:

- status
- next action
- next follow-up date
- objection or decision blocker if any
- proposal status if applicable

---

## Delivery QA

Confirm every approved project has:

- approved scope
- exclusions
- assets needed
- access needed
- approval contact
- test plan
- launch conditions
- post-launch check date

---

## Chapter 133 field script

> If the dashboard cannot tell us what the lead needs, what to recommend, what not to promise, and what to do next, it needs to be updated.

Bridge question:

> Which field is missing that would prevent a clean sale or delivery handoff?

---

## Chapter 133 training check

A team member passes this chapter if they can audit a lead and know whether the dashboard has enough information.

They fail if they ignore missing guardrails or next actions.

# The AI Plug Master Manual v3 — Part 14: Delivery, Implementation + Launch QA
**AI Advantage First operating system section**  
**Date:** 2026-05-27

**Manual type:** Full-depth delivery and operations training manual  
**Section covered:** Part 14 — Delivery, Implementation + Launch QA

## Upload note

`THE_AI_PLUG_MASTER_MANUAL_V3_COMPLETE_2026-05-27.md`

## Direction lock for this section

This section follows the corrected AI Advantage First direction.

Delivery must not treat The AI Plug as a normal website shop, chatbot installer, form builder, or generic automation service.

Delivery must build the first useful AI system the client actually bought.

That means every project must protect:

- business reality
- approved scope
- service lane
- vertical language
- guardrails
- client approvals
- user experience
- mobile-first quality
- safe AI behavior
- owner/staff handoff
- post-launch learning
- monthly improvement path

The delivery standard is:

# Build the practical AI advantage the client approved — not random features, not overbuilt systems, not unsafe automation.
